O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	I have completed this book for you, my very dear son, which is the end of the knowledge of medicine along with its fullness, and I have finished it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I will complete this for you with this treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is corrupted in our region and is foreign to everyone in everything, science and learning perish and are destroyed, and there remains nothing of them except small descriptions in books by the ancients that the hands have altered.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this [comes] error and vanity; intentions are closed off and knowledge is driven away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I shall revive [it] together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of cautery instruments, as well as other tools for work, along with the alignment of the declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good craftsmen are found in our times, the art of medicine has become distant.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who undertakes it should be summoned in the knowledge of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the judgment of members, and their shapes and joints and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and sinews and the number of bones, and their movement and those that move and those that rest, and the direction of their outflow.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason Hippocrates says that a name without work is nothing, and the same applies to the art of healing.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that one who is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, should be careful so as not to err and not to harm people; in such a way that I have seen many times that those who engage in this science and abandon their science and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish man who cut open one abscess of scrofula or the throat of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck; therefore so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in her hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another man who drew a stone from an old man, and the stone was large; with it he carried away a piece of the bladder, and the man died within four days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat it, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they cut it, he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And there was another physician who took care of one of the duke of our land, who had his leg broken and with the break came an injury; and the physicians, full of ignorance, pulled the break over the wound by strong force, and did not leave any splint on the wound, but let it be thus set; and he commanded that it should not be dislocated again; and it remained so until the leg became completely swollen and the toes and came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and dislocate the leg; and when I dislocated it, it was peaceful and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the corruption had already been confirmed in the limb, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not stop spreading through the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And another eye that collapses an abscess and then inflames it through the evil of its dominion.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For when the chancre is purged of melancholic humor, it should not be touched with iron unless it is in a place where all can be removed that is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: one where there is danger in many positions; and I will show in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore it is necessary that you take care, so that the foolish eye cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you take up your weapons in cushioning, and approach your patients gently and firmly, and use the best way, so that through God's grace you may come to salvation and be praised; and leave behind the diseases full of great suffering; and remove your weapons from those that cause doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can depart from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen warned in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on bad illnesses, lest you be called foolish physician."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauterization and the cauterization of medicine for ague, and it is arranged from head to toes; and about the shapes of instruments, and the devices for cauterizing, and everything necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and abscesses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and it is arranged and the shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is arranged from head to toes, and about the shapes of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, as we remember our work, it is necessary that I tell the quality of aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid, and the harm, is the longest and most subtle speech and secret responses; and many wise men spoke of it, and agreed with this; and they relied little on their words, because I will reduce the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally to all complexions where there is matter, whether it be of the two complexions: hot with matter and dry with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a hot and dry complexion, some people said that cautery is great help; and others said the opposite: that cautery has no value for disease caused by heat and drought.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot and should not be used to treat hot diseases with heat or drought; and this is what those who said the opposite claim: that cautery provides great help for hot and dry diseases in humans.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	If you understand the body of a man and its moisture according to the nature of fire, you will find it cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it sometimes through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, do not interfere unless one who has tested it, and who knows through long experience the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of men's constitutions, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the occurrences and space of time; we have no fear from other constitutions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all should submit themselves to the cautery treatment.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, sons, that cautery together with fire is one of the secrets of cures, and of greater kindness than cauterization with hot medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple and does not harm any other member except the one it touches.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Hot medicines spread from one member to another when they are applied, and cause illness of grave healing; and by chance, the patient may die.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its highness and the kindness of its substance, does not do this if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have discovered this for you through experiment and by the length of service and study that I have put into my art, and it is true concerning the things; therefore, I apologize for the length of the words, for I do not wish to deprive you of the secret which concerns fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives off diseases from the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; accept this in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, that they agreed on what time the cauteries should be performed and chose their companions.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that the cautery is suitable in all times, because the harm occurring is kept under control by the aid of the cautery; and indeed, if the cauteries are necessary for pain relief, it cannot be postponed until a more serious illness comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think about it, dear child, as the foolish do; for a disease cured by cautery has no return; and they say so; but it is not as they believe, because cauteries are not medicine that changes complexion, but rather dries humors causing pain, and works more quickly than other medicine due to its power and its virtue.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	It is possible that the disease sometimes comes according to the complexion of the patient and the nature of the disease and its virtue; and superfluidities are gathered in him through the consumption of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are administered where there is little superfluity or moisture, as in cauterization for pain, and similar things; but this does not happen often.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the end of medicine, but it is true; however, they do not believe that cauteries are more effective after other medicines, but their belief is false; cauteries are the last resort in medicine because when we administer methods of cures for any disease and they are not effective, then we administer cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cauteries are at the rear of medicine, not according to the intentions of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauteries made of gold are more effective than those of iron, and they said this not because of the quality of gold or the highness of its substance; but rather they claimed that the tips of cauteries do not produce pus, but it is not true since I have tested it, and found that it is true in some men; and cauteries made of gold are more effective than those of iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know if it is hot by the color of gold, and sometimes it cools down quickly; and if you heat it too much, it burns; and thus there are many impediments to this.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cautery which we have adapted to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have instructed you on this chapter about the head from the neck to the feet, because the path is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for both hot and cold conditions of the brain, and it is used due to a disease known as "soda," and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and because of numerous dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and most importantly, for all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a medicinal solution, clearing the head four times or twice, according to what the qualities and age and condition of the sick person can tolerate; and then you make an incision at the back of the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then make the patient sit cross-legged between your hands and put his hands on something; afterward, place the base of your palm over the root of his nose between his two eyes; and where your fingers will meet, it bleeds from there. Then heat the cautery called "olivare," which is the shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it on the place marked with ink, and do so while pressing and pulling your hand little by little, turning it over; then lift your hand immediately if you see the bone sticking out a little bit; if you don't see it, continue the cautery until you see the bone as I told you; afterwards take a piece of silk, put it in warm water and soft cotton inside, put it on the place, and leave it for three days; afterwards put a thin linen cloth soaked in butter on it; leave it there until the burn is healed; afterwards heal the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said, when an overwound (or ulcer) remains open longer, it drains more; and for this reason, let it be dressed (treated).
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some said that the cautery (treatment involving fire) should be allowed to burn a part of the bone and then the burnt part of the bone should be removed and healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that the cautery (treatment involving fire) should be applied strongly so as to break the bone as wide as one vertebra that women put in their vaginas because the humors issue out more freely; and then the wound should be left open for a long time; after that, it should be healed and bandaged.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two types of cauteries do not seem good to me in all respects, except for certain people who have fear; and it seems to me that I should let them be; because the heads are weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we witness with other limbs; and even when the head of the patient is naturally weak, the first appearance of cautery seems more healing and beneficial to me, and in this way, I work for the sake of safety.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the head has chronic and long-lasting pain, the patient should use ear drops and pills called "cochie," and purge of the head, oils, and plasters; and if one performs cautery on it as we have said before, it is of no value.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's shoulder is of strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize beneath it with that fire cautery as we have said before.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Perform cauterization on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and perform one cautery or treatment called "vasselz"; it is one of the two in which ventouses are placed; hold your hand so you do not see beyond the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will speak more about it later; and the cauterizations on the horns should be subtler than those used for the middle of the head, and this is their form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the head cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in one part of the head and the disease spreads to the eyes, and the head is purged by various medicines, and other treatments as I have said in the division of diseases are performed but none help; then cauterization is done according to two methods: namely, with hot medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with hot medicine is that you take an onion and peel the skin off it, and put one piece of onion at each eye where the pain is, in such a way that you can place the onion under the skin; and when it is placed, press it well and leave it for twelve hours; then remove the onion and treat the area with salt for two or three days, and then cover it with linen dipped in butter as long as it lasts.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the onion treatment until it is healed; and if you see that this does not help, perform one of the treatments with burning medicines that I have written or the tenth treatment for burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cautery is of this kind. Heat the iron according to these forms:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	It is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a claw or has one and a half inches of curvature, and it is medium-sized with a small appearance; place it on the painful spot, hold your hand firmly and slightly tap the iron, so that half the thickness of the tip is burned; lift your hand to prevent the artery from burning, and draw out the abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing cotton on a piece of linen, place it for four days; then put damp cotton in vinegar, and then treat the spot with ointment until it heals; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the iron called "cultellare", prick it entirely, but be careful not to pierce the artery in this migraine that is not old.
de emigraine	From migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When curing migraine as previously mentioned in the divisions of diseases, and it does not benefit from the cauteries mentioned in medicine and iron, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it becomes white; and so place it on the side of the temple along a line of half a finger's length, and press once with your hand, but do not cover the artery nor let the pressure reach the bone; protect the jawbone from mute people when they eat, and let the veins have no regard for the mute and prevent spasmus from coming to the patient, and protect against discharge of blood from the artery when it is cut, or when cutting have great fear and especially to those who do not know, and are unstudied and inexperienced; leave the procedure in progress; but I will tell you how to stop the flow of blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it should be in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not help the disease and the patient is suffering, cauterize it on the head as previously mentioned, and treat the wound until it heals; and if you see, administer the cautery we have said or the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	Of the pain of the ears from coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from coldness and it has been treated with soluble medicines and other remedies as we have said in the division, and the pain does not subside, then apply this cautery called 'poins', which is made as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After piercing the affected ear all around, or in both places where the pain is located, move away slightly from the root of the ear once you have marked the place to be treated; have ten points around each ear; treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	The torment to be cured by cautery is not foreign to those that move from flux, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not perform cautery on the similar cases that come from scorch and from spasm of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this similar torment that stops flux from the ears and cleansing of the head and gargarism, and this does not suffice, then you must cauterize the patient with four cauteries: one in the root of the ear, and another a little distance away from the temple, and the third at the corner of the lips; place the cautery in the open healthy part and make it cauterize towards the top of the ear slightly below the skull, and another in the temple as long as a thumb; and let the cautery stay until half of the coal is burned; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is similar to the surgeon's tool that we have mentioned, but it is somewhat more delicate and requires the knife to be slightly larger; after curing the wound as I have previously said, let it heal when it becomes healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, but it does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then perform four cauterizations: two on the top of the forehead, one in the skull, and one at the vessel called "vasselz" as I have previously mentioned, and the last cauterization on the stomach's mouth; let them be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	diarrhea
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, give the patient large years and round pills to the brain; after that, anoint the head of the patient all over, and place the plaster of mustard (made from sinapi) on top of the occipital bone. This is the method of cautery: if you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy in this manner, it is good; and if not, make four cauteries on the head descending from neck to collarbone, and have space between each cautery of two large ones; and cure as with others, and if you see it heal, give one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two more on the two horns, and cure until it is healthy; and let the cauteries that are called "olivare" be as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the chill in the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head (of the patient) be cleaned with years and whatever was said before; after cleaning the patient's head, then make the cautery in the head and on each horn, one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if there is a need for more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is severe, make four cauteries on the spine of the back; and let it be until the most painful spot is burned, then remove your hand; afterwards, cure it until it is healed, and let the cautery which is called "olivare" that was said before be used.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cautery except for those who are febrile, and it is necessary first to clean the brain with years and other treatments as was said in the division when the patient is large and suffering from taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot endure it, give him gargling and chewing frequently with soft food; afterwards, put the head in a millstone, and apply 1 cautery as described before, and 1 cautery on the fontanelle, and on each cornea; and if the patient is weak and tolerant, apply cauteries as I have said to him who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped as I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, apply a gentle cautery in the following manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When caused by melancholy are the superfluidities or corrupt and swollen fluids, then cauterize with such cauteries as we have said to him who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the superfluidity is declining towards melancholy and the body of the patient is moist, then give them to drink something by which the brain may be purified, according to what was mentioned before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place the patient cross-legged; then make a linen bandage well made, like a circle, and put it around the head; and the patient should be crossed, and held firmly from all sides; after this apply the liner, and rub with old butter; and heat it gently at fire so that it can be applied without causing discomfort to the patient; afterwards remove the circle inside the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient every week once with good management, until they are well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	If you see that the patient is to be cauterized by making multiple pricks over the entire cautery, this method moistens the brain greatly; then place damp cotton soaked in butter and linseed oil on top of it.
de l’awe des eulz	Of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyes come first by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and give the patient something purifying the head, and protect it from all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe more often while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterwards, command him to rest his head and make a fire cautery on the head, and make two cauteries on the temples where the eyelid swelling is on both eyes or one eye; and pierce all the veins and arteries that are under the eyebrow, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and watch for bleeding, and if you see too much blood flowing, stop it with your power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of the arteries and in the incision the cautery how to stop it; and sometimes they make a fire cautery or heat something under the two bones at the back.
dou cors des larmes	The tears of the body (translated from Old French)
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the eyes become old and accustomed to being on the veins, or from the arteries that are visible on the outside of the head; and it is seen that this is due to cold phlegmatic superfluities, then let him perform the cautery as I have said at the beginning of the chapter, namely: cautery in the head, two cauteries on the temples, two cauteries or cauterizations under the eyes, and if necessary, cauterize skillfully above the eyebrows with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	The tears of the body within the eyes (translated from Old French)
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat the patient according to what we have said in the division, but it does not help, then give a sick person three nux vomica (poison nuts); after that, roast the head and do a olive oil cautery or millet cautery; and make two cauterizations called "clavilis" over the two sores, one beneath the hair; be careful not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called “clavilis”:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then do this type of cautery called “olivary.” Here is its form:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish to perform two cauterizations on the two sorcerers who are as long as sorcerers are; and do not leave the hand except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair which pricks the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes the hair of the oils are transformed into a burn and prick the oil, and one performs cauterization in two ways: either by fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they have grown even and long, then place the patient on a paper with the hairs marked out in the shape of the myrtle leaf, and begin the sign at the base of the hairs; then put damp cotton soaked in egg white and mustard oil on the oil, then heat the cautery to this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing over the marked shape repeatedly, so that the edges are burned; and the signs of the cure's success are that you see the paper withdrawn, and the hairs raised at the tip of the oil; then lift your hand, and let it be for four days, then put damp cotton in butter until the cautery is removed; afterwards heal with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after that the hairs grow, and the paper is softened, then repeat the fire cautery on the same place as before; and if the hairs are curved, cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural position and even, and the hairs do not prick oil out.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The hot cautery in medicine is to instruct the patient to let their hairs grow long and even, then make parchment of the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and hot metal, one ounce of each, grind them together well; and do this quickly, so it does not cool; then spread on the form you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and put the parchment over the hairs; if the sickness only has one oil drop, work with one, and if in both; put cotton dampened with egg white underneath the oil; and the shoulder of the patient should be healthy and your finger should be on top showing the medicine, and press once and move it all each time the patient feels a bite from the medicine, for it bites like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done that for a long time, remove the medicine from your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the bite has healed, lift up the affected area and check if the pus has been released as it was lifted by fire or incision; and if this is the case, then it is good. If not, apply more medicine to the area or where no medicine has worked yet, until your treatments are even, and your eyes focused; then put moist cotton on it in butter until the wound burns shut, afterwards cure the area with the ointment called "dyafenis" and another one until it heals.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if you need to be careful in your treatment because the medicine is not sticking to the hairs.  If the pus becomes thick and the hairs prick in the oil, then repeat the application of medicine to that area which has been properly softened by the pus, as you have done before; afterwards cure it until it heals; and this is the shape of a comfrey leaf.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the hair of men is diverse in size and smallness, and according to this you should adjust your treatments; and do not deviate from the correct way for those who are studying this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When treating a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases and your treatment does not help, then you must perform cautery on it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put their head in a basin of warm water or near hot coals, and have the assistant hold the patient's head between their hands so it does not move or shake; after putting cotton moistened with egg white or soap and oil on the fistula, heat the cautery to the required temperature, making it shaped like the tip of a feather and attached to the cautery. If you wish, the cautery can be pointed from one side to the other, or as wide as a tent; but regardless, the former is more suitable for your task.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it is open, drain the pus and dry it; if it is closed, open it and remove the scab; after placing the hot cautery on top, hold your hand on the cautery to the affected area near the oil, being careful not to make a mistake; place the cautery in the oil and burn it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you start the cautery up to the bone, it would be good. If not, restart the cauterization again once, and another time if needed, and leave it for 3 days; afterwards put cotton soaked in butter on it, and let the ointment drying treatment continue until it heals, and if 40 days pass without healing, put corrosive medicine on the exposed bone; and the king according to what is stated in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients mentioned. Understand a fistula, and cut the area; afterwards put one subtle camahan in the opening, which is shaped as follows:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make the amount of one piece of lead; hold your hand firmly with camahan, and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted lead flows into its hole; it is necessary to put oil on the patient's cotton soaked in egg yolk or butter: the lead will heal the fistula and the wound miraculously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good. If not, you must administer pepper to the nose and bring the fistula back into the heat of the nose as required in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	cavities in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there are cavities in lips called "hair", and even in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When curing these cavities as we have said in sections, and the cure is not effective, then heat. I.e., a small cautery scalpel according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put him immediately into those cavities until he comes to the font; afterward, treat the wound with lime until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the eye, or palate, or roots of the teeth, after it becomes pus-filled and grows and turns into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not help: then it is necessary that you have .i. cautery according to the size of the fistula; after letting out or piercing the fistula, hold your hand until the iron becomes hot at the source of it, and where the end is; and do this once or twice, after curing what we have said in treatments, until it is healthy; and if it is cured thus, it is good; but if not, you must discover the place and remove the corrupt bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	The double movement of teeth (or teeth grinding)
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines but they do not improve, then place the head of the patient in hot water; afterwards, apply a heated cautery to the tooth in this manner: put a cane on the tooth; and insert the heated cautery quickly, keep your hand so that the patient feels the heat approaching the root of the tooth; after releasing your hand, continue the cauterization according to your will; afterwards fill the mouth of the patient with salt water, and bind it tightly for an hour and rinse thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the moving tooth is fixed and the gums are kept soft and moistures dried up.
de la dolor des dens	Of the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from coldness, or there is coldness or fever, and the medicines do not help, then there should be need of cautery according to two ways: cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery with butter is as follows: take butter from a cow, and the end in an iron or copper spoon; after that take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a needle, then wet it in boiled butter and apply it immediately to the painful tooth and hold it until it cools down; repeat this often until its property reaches the root of the tooth. If you see the linen and cotton getting cold in the boiled butter, apply it again, but heat one hot iron next to the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	1. The cauteries altogether are made with a rod of iron or brass, and it should be thick so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth; heat the cautioner, from which the form will come after, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled; do this often, for the pain will be relieved that day itself or the next.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	3. And make the cautioner at whichever place you wish, and according to your ability; and this is the shape of the rod.
des scrophules	of scrofula (a chronic skin disease)
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrophulas are of a fluid and cold moisture, and do not respond to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery hair as follows comes the shape, and make two openings for the smoke to exit from the other part; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the base of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it as such for three days; and put soft cotton soaked in butter until the sore is healed; afterward cure the place with ointments and plasters until it is healed.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the coldness prevails on the channel of the worm, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must first be purged with soluble medicines; afterward apply cautery at the root of the throat, but do not go near the throat, only a little bit. Afterward make one other cautery at the jointure of the neck to the head of the spine, and let it be the cautery that is called "clavicle" as we have the form before; and cure the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the tooth
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and illness of worm are from cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or inflammation, and the disease is ancient, you should make two cauterizations on the forearm; and another cautery between the breasts; and let it be the cautery called "clavile" in the form as was said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a .xxx., ou enqui entor. Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a .iij. rains selonc ceste forme:	And if you wish, make a cautery by pricking all along the cautery that is called "point" in the form given for ear disease; and let the points be up to 30 or around it. After curing the place as was said before, let the cautery be at four fingers distance according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because the cauterizations are lighter, because you make them in pairs (two).
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After being attentive to the patient on his back and on his side; after locating the cavity that is within the hole with your left hand's tip; and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery which has two nerves as shown here:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the cavity until it penetrates to the costal cartilage, and the figure of the cautery consists of four cauteries; and for this reason, caution is taken with the cautery that has two nerves, because the shapes of cauterization are these cauteries; and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tent and this is the shape of the cautery that has two nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is dislocated on this, namely the nerve, for which there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After apply the cautery to crush with oil; after make the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for long time until it is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant. Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	If it is dislocated above, which happens seldom, then do cautery on the thick part of the cautery clavicle, or many cauteries in pricking. For the jointure is restored, and moisture is removed, and the patient recovers.
dou cautere de pleuresin	the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancient ones said that for pleurisy, one should apply fire cauteries made from roots of aristolochia, and in this manner: take a long root of aristolochia, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and also as large and as long as your thumb; wet it in oil, heat it up, and then cauterize one cautery between the chest and neck, and two small cauteries a little downwards in the area below the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining slightly behind a little; one cautery on the side of the liver, and another above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two at the sides of the liver away from the cautery which is between the two shoulders; and do not squeeze your hand tightly, but perform it as freely as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	And they said that a certain old man uses a cautery resembling a razor and heats it up and places it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; then the pain subsides as we have said in the liver abscess. However, in this work there is fear or death for many patients now, or fistula occurs which cannot be cured.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mice, that is, leprosy, as we have said in the treatments, and it does not improve, then present three ways of cautery, all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	The first method is that you make four or six cauteries in a line according to the length of the leprosy, according to the figure of the liver cautery as we have said before; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient remain conscious on his back.
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery with two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and shave the hair that is towards the leprosy, where the patient's growth comes towards his left side, and the elevations from which you shave the hair should be according to the length of the body, and the cautery should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the two inflamed nerves are heated until the boil is pierced from the other side, then pull out the cautery, and so there will be four. And if you see, if you cauterize all the cauteries at three nerves. After healing when it has discharged pus for a long time, and this is worth noting that the other treatments mentioned before should be done first.
de ydropisie	After heating with sulphur or brimstone until it burns, then apply to the place of the boil; and if you see that the abscess is filled with pus, then open it carefully without hurting the healthy flesh; and after cleaning the wound, let it be covered with honey or oil.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	Cauterization is not suitable for boils, except in the manner that is called "asclytes". When you treat it according to the methods we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not help, then you must do four cauteries around the boil, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two at the back near the spine, and one at the place of the pain; and let the cauteries be close to the thick part of the skin.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the fire cautery open to purge for a long time, do not neglect the care of the patient after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will be together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the abdomen is the clavicle as we have shown before; and that for the back is olive-shaped, as it is described above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner. Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	When the feet are swollen in someone who is edema-ridden, and they are full of that yellow matter, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and take your hand with the cautery without turning. And do not enter too deep, so as not to penetrate the yellow matter excessively, and let the cautery be in this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After doing two cauteries in each leg with the point of the knife; and let the cautery be long, one below the knee in front and the other outside the leg; leave the cauteries over it for a long time to heal, until the yellow matter disappears; after healing the other wounds as we have said.
de la menoison	of the emaciation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the belly solution comes from coldness and moisture, while the digestive and retentive virtues in the stomach and intestine are obstructed and cannot be cured by means of treatment; and you see the patient suffering greatly and of strong constitution, do this: apply one large cautery on the stomach as described before (cautery of the stomach), around the navel circulate; and four subtle cauteries all around the abdomen, one subtle cautery clavicle, and two cauteries on the flanks.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, do cautery on the joints (of the limb) and one cautery on each joint, and two small cauteries on the stomach under the large one, because the treatment is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
