Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are founded, either one or more, and are old and are of large, cold, corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in the divisions, and it does not help if you make cauteries: 4 on the spine of the back, that which is entirely exposed below the vertebrae and protrudes triangularly, and 1 cautery under the navel. 2 times;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that his stomach is cooled and the meat does not cook, and the face swells, then do one large cautery on the stomach as mentioned earlier, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen entirely to the clavicle; and leave the cautery open for a long time. After healing the place until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the hernia called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you apply the cautery to althelul, heat up the cautery that seems like a razor, and then place it all over the althelul to be cauterized; leave your hand there so that the cautery reaches the opening of the vein, so as not to miss it. Do this once or twice, and if there is much althelul, cauterize each one as we have said; after that, heal with ointments until they are healthy; and if you cauterize a large cautery on alchatim, it will have more help.
de plaie mal curee	from an improperly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear incision or opening, as we will explain in its place, this disease comes which cannot be cured except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	1. When a fistula comes, and it is swollen and filled with pus and corrupt moisture, you should probe its entire length with a subtle instrument, and be aware of how deep it goes entirely.
de la maladie des reins	17. Here is the translation for the next sentence:
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain in the loins and severe swelling comes from the kidneys, and it does not take on female characteristics, then you should perform cautery over the kidneys on both sides with the cautery as previously mentioned; and if we cauterize it in the middle, it will have 4 cauteries in a line, and it will provide more help.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder becomes weak and soft from cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then make a fire cautery in the area beyond the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one on the right side and one on the left side, and both should be as long as one's thumb; and make one incision behind the back, or two if necessary; and make the cauteries sharp according to the shape previously described.
de la marris	of the marriage
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marriage is cold and moist and does not allow conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their term is delayed; and when they come, there is great pain: then it is necessary to do four cauterizations around the womb, as we have said in the treatment of the bladder, and two cauterizations behind the back; and make the cauteries sharp, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the haunch
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous fluids descend into the joint of the haunch and cause it to become immobile, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the joint's location can be observed by sight, if necessary you should cauterize the patient over the joint of the haunch with a cautery resembling a circle, and sign in front of the joint around the area, so that the area is within the circle; and the cauterization should be similar to that used for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, make four large olive-shaped cauterizations, and the cauterizations should be as deep as all the wounds; and heal it until it is healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the haunch
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the loin of the haunch, and it is due to coldness and moisture; the patient is treated as we have said in the division, but the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After performing the cautery; and the method of the cautery is according to two methods: namely with burning medications, or cauterization by fire. Cauterization by fire has many ways, one of which is as follows: you should cauterize on the loin of the haunch four triangular cauteries according to this shape, and make a deep and wide incision between each cautery with the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes cauterization is made in the middle of the loin over the head of the haunch, so there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, perform the fire cautery on the circular cauterizer mentioned earlier in the dislocation of the thigh; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire thigh, and all the flesh around the wound is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is how one performs sciatica when the pain is in the thigh and does not reach the thigh or leg. If it reaches the thigh and the leg, do two cauterizations where the patient says that the pain is located, and one cautery below the ankle on the left side a little; let the cauteries be a scalpel-type, and burn the flesh around the wound; if the patient feels that the pain extends to the foot or close to it, cauterize where they feel the pain at four fingers or four cauteries called "fingers."
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	If necessary, do more; and if the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, perform a cautery with a scalpel-type or circular cauterizer, and be careful in all your cauterizations that you do not burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who made cautery on the ankle bone of the foot, and they left it for so long that the leg swelled completely, and the toes also, and all the toes were pierced and corrupted. After a belly solution from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two places together, make cautery in one and the other, as follows. // And the wise will say in the cautery of the shin, as follows: Make one iron rod the same size as a small nail of a finger, or slightly smaller, and it should be between-cheeks or from one between-cheek to the other at a distance equal to a nut of a thumb; and the between-cheeks should be above two parts, and they should resemble nuts, and have one iron handle well made; and this is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Heat it up until it is all red and boiling hot, and then place it on the sick person's shin, turning it towards the healthy side; and cauterize once with one iron rod and leave for four days; then apply a plaster of butter, leaving the wound open for a long time; afterwards cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says we should use little of this fire cautery due to fear of its gaze, and few use it; however, this is one of the good cauterizations that can endure it, where it scorches.
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When back pain comes from falling, or blows, or excessive bleeding, or similar causes of cold matter spreading, none of these cases are worth using cauterization except for the one that comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary afterwards that the patient is voided of foul pills or similar things, which are placed on the back where the pain is, three lines signed with ink, and in each line five cauteries or more according to the potency and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cautery should be done according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, do four cauteries or four according to the moderately sharp cautery in this manner:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have narrow anus when they defecate, and fear; and you find it in the lower spine on the back and in its appearance which comes over other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you wish to cure it, cauterize it with the cautery of that kind in this manner.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	The cautionery must increase in each part of the spine. And if you see, cauterize around the spine with the pointed cautionery 2 or 3 lines, and the tips should be close to each other. Afterwards cure the place until it is healthy according to what we have said, and take care that you do not administer cautionery in a gilbositeit (a condition of swelling or inflammation) which is in the nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	For the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of the joints is due to moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which are called "podagre" properly, and when it is caused by cold and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured with cauteries in this manner: make a large amount of cautionery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautionery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary for you to press on the foot, make a fire cautery all over the cautery mark "point". And if the pains come up to the knee and at other joints, and this happens frequently, make a fire cautery on each knee. Four cauteries or four on each part, an olive oil cautery all over; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand beyond the burned area.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knees and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. If the pain is in the hands, do the pricking around the fleshy part two lines; and if there remains no pain in the fingers, do pricking on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if pains come up to the wrists or shoulders, cauterize each part, and care for the patient well and consider medicines. For if you provide good care and purge phlegm, it will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the siphac
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When ruptures come in anger, and the intestines descend into the abdomen and it is newly formed, if you wish to cure it, it should not be touched that day; and it should be treated with things that relax the stomach, so that the intestines descend from the stomach. After doing this, make the patient sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm straight until the rupture is repaired, and bend them at your elbows, and press firmly on the site of the rupture above the wrist bone, and at a sign that resembles half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery according to this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and gives off heat signs. Then reposition the intestines to their place; and have the minister place his hand where they do not return; and work well the thighs on the patient, and put one cushion and one belt around the thighs, and another on the affected part that holds the hands; then put the cautery on the sign with your whole hand, and hold it straight and until you reach the bone, and if you do not touch it the first time, try again until you reach the bone; be careful not to let the intestines rise when you apply the cautery; do not burn them; and thus the patient may not die or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is of no value. It should be noted that the cauteries for children are fine according to their size, and those for adults according to theirs; after three days cure the wound from the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; afterwards cure it with other remedies until it heals, and lie the patient on his back for forty days until the wound is well sutured; and his excrements should be loosened so that the intestines do not rise when he wishes to go to the chamber.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when it wants to get up, bring a well-made bandage and keep it for forty more days; let it have good rest, that it does not work too much or drink too much or eat too much, and does not shout too loudly; and if it follows this instruction, it will be healed entirely. And I will say afterwards the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the wound from the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When wounds appear in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow more, make one cautery of the cautery according to its size, and it should be burned the third part of the belly; afterwards cure as we have said; and no one of the ancients has said that it should be cauterized with a cautery at four angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But first, mark the location of the dislocation and make a line above the incision site, and another below, and place your hand on top of the entire cautery tool. However, the first cauteries are lighter and more mobile.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain occurs in any limb, be it from a fall or an injury, and this pain lasts a long time, and medicine does not cure it, therefore it should be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cautery should be according to the length of the member, its smallness and weakness, and its virtue and location of twisting and of its pain. If it heals from the first cautery, that is good; but if not, start another cautery on top of it, as this is the custom, because the caution should move towards the limb that is closer, so you must make the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	Of mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Mixtures are sometimes treated with cautionery, and similarly the sickness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you wish to cauterize it, take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not descend nor remain; if you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the sickness, then perform five cauteries on the head: one on the forehead at the end of the hairline; two on the temples; one behind the ear; and one on the nose, leaving your hand so that the cautery reaches the bone, and so that the scabs come out from it, so that the vapors of the gross humors may escape; and cauterize the eye according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mixture is scattered everywhere, it manifests clearly that you must cauterize it with the cauteries that we have said on the head, and one cautery in the neck, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the buttock and one other near it, and two on the hips; and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the feet, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are above the last ribs, lest you burn them; and sometimes do a cautery on the bone of the fist, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	1. And know that the more you perform cautery, the more help it provides and benefits [the patient]; and know that sick people feel no pain during cauterization as healthy people do, because the body is already completely corrupted.
de enfleure	When the body part swells due to moisture, it should be treated with a poultice made from various herbs and applied for several days or nights as needed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling appears in any body part and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but it is not healed, then cautery should be performed on the affected member according to its size and smallness. The cauterization should be shallow, about the thickness of a fingernail. After that, heal it with ointments until it is healed. Occasionally, cautery is done on the hand, foot, or back at the location where a nerve is silent, which removes the swelling; however, no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about body parts and the movement of nerves in the body.
de albaras	From the sling (or bandage)
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the illness called "albaras" appears, and medical instruments are of no use, then cauterize it with a small hot iron, according to the thickness of the wound skin, until the blister is removed and its color changes; then treat it with flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, as well as the blood of a pig and the blood of an almond, each in turn; mix everything together, tie it up with a cloth, and apply it to the wound until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of syphilis by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When an abscess begins and you want to stop it, if you cauterize with the cautery that seems like a circle around the edge of the abscess. And yet wise men say that cautionery should be done in the middle of the abscess; and yet I do not think this is good, because I fear it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen once before; and a more appropriate thing is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circular", as we have said in terms of cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	the inflammation that cannot grow larger
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", which grows slowly due to the excess it produces, or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (meaning very old) and has little blood, or for some other reason; if you want to make it grow faster: then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking it; afterwards leave it as such. Because it will stop growing.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced through and through with the fire-cautery, then heat the fire-cautery as described here:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of that illness called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced through the skin, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels the heat spread throughout his body in such a way that the course of the purgation is clear. Afterward, heal it perfectly when it is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	treatment with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another method of illness is called "corrodens," and it is nothing but an eating away of a limb, for it consumes the limbs as fire dries up dry wood. If you see this disease in a place that can be treated with cautery along with fire, then heat the cauteries, both small and large, according to the place or location where the illness is; after the cauterization of all parts until all corruption is removed, and nothing remains of it, cut out everything that is corrupt. And leave it for three days, and put on top of the cauterized places soft ointment made with oil until the burns from the fire are healed, and all corruption is removed. After the cure by poultices produces new skin. If after three days you see that healthy skin does not grow, that is good; if not, then repeat the cautery on the remaining corrupt parts. And this eating away is sometimes cured with medicine made of garlic instead of fire-cautery; but nevertheless, fire-cautery is more effective, and I have already discussed the cure for medicine made of garlic in another section: take it when needed.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The hairs which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often a disease called "claw" occurs on the feet according to our understanding, which is a large thing that claws the foot. And the cauterization of this disease is in two ways. That is to say, cauterization by fire and cauterization by hot water. Cauterization by fire is that you heat one cautery like a feather of a quill, made of good iron as much as it can penetrate the nail on all sides, and there should be subtle margins; after that place it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the base of the nail; and leave it like this for four days until it begins to emit pus; then make an ointment of foul herbs boiled with oil, and leave the ointment over everything all night, and the nail will shrink and be removed from its roots. Then cure the place with warming liniment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	If it is converted on the outside of the body and often occurs in hands and feet, then you should bring hot cauterization; and it is done in this way: take a cane of wax or iron, or a feather of quill, and put it over the nail and apply it to the warts (hairs); and place the cane so that it presses all around, then put a small amount of hot oil on it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand in turning so that the edges of the cane reach the root of the nail, and may find the hot oil penetrating to the root; and allow the patient to bear the bite of the hot oil for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will be removed from all its roots. Repeat this until you have burned all those on the body, then cure them with liniments that warm up.
li cure dou trembler	The Cure for Trembling (literally: "the trembling care")
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	For some who tremble from coldness of the nerves or from quarter fever or any other illness, you should perform four or five cauterizations on the spine of the back, one between each vertebra; and one at the navel, and one above the stomach with the olive cautery; this will stop the trembling, and the healthiness will hasten away from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	Putrid boils (literally: "smelly pustules")
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	At times, the body shows swellings filled with foul pus that come from corrupted substances. When they appear, it is necessary to perform a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery made from a stick of myrtle, so that the tip can be heated by fire, or a long root of arsenic, or the cauterizing cauterizer. And sometimes they are cauterized at their beginning when they appear, following this method, and they cannot grow further, but the superfluous parts from which they come are destroyed, and they become healthy; however, it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	At times, there are great discharges of blood from the cut artery that comes at an open wound or abscess incision, or to a cauterized limb, and similar things; it is a very serious matter to allow this to flow out.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And furthermore, whenever this happens, hasten to place your finger on the vein wound, and hold it very tightly until the blood is stopped from flowing; then take olive oil cauteries, both small and large, until they are all red; then take one, either large or small depending on the wound and where the artery is located; and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stopped flowing.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	If the vein jumps when you hold your finger on it and the cautery stops, take hastily another one of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And continue to do this one after another until the blood is stopped flowing; and beware not to burn the nerve that is exposed, and no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when the artery does not stop bleeding, it cannot be well stopped when the artery is large, unless this is done by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it has not been treated, or by tightly tying a thread, or by medicines placed on it that have the power to stop bleeding; and it should be tied and held in place accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever applies tight bandages or places hot things on it, or similar things, will not benefit from it unless otherwise.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens and there is no medicine or remedy present, then put your finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it tightly over the wound and the vein; do not move it but wet it with cold water often until the wound is very cold, frozen, swollen, and held in place; and follow the instructions for cauteries and medicines that are needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgery
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every disease in which fire cautery or a burning medicine is required, and about their kinds, causes, instruments, forms of cauteries; and I have placed that chapter up to the feet, and I will go into this chapter through the same way because it will be easier for you to find those things that you are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so as I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to be foolish, because many people come for treatment. Some of them are so afflicted by their disease that they die easily from the madness they find due to their illness and the great severity of it; and this should be feared.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And there are some who give their sense and say: "Wait, I am cured"; but the illness is deceitful. You should not consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more trust in your honor than in your desire, and do not act recklessly but wisely regarding those of whom you are certain, and from which you can have experience; and use diagnosis and prognosis in the treatment of your patients to bring salvation; and this will help you acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dearest son, Our Lord grants you good understanding and righteousness, and if you desire to inspire by the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have organized this chapter in sections, as it is set out according to the chapter of cauteries, which I have previously explained from head to foot because you will find it easier to understand what is necessary.
dou chief plein d’aigue	full head swollen with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often comes to children at birth, and sometimes it happens for reasons unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and all that I have seen hasten to death; therefore it seems to me worthwhile to abandon the work in some treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose neck was filled with water and his head swelled every day until he could no longer bear it; the moisture gathered under the skull bone between the skull and the bone; and since the moisture is between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make an incision large in the head; and let it be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture can pass; and here is the form of a lancet:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the abscesses are larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone and you see the joints at the head of each part opening wide when pressed with your hand from within, and it does not respond to you: you must make three incisions in the head of the joint like this:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After the incision remove all moisture from it. Then apply dressings and powders to the incisions and pour wine and oil on them and leave it like that for five days; then dislocate it, and care for the wound by bandaging and ointmenting, and let the joint stretch gradually, and give the patient dry meat of a moist animal until the limb is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you observe the size of the abscess and its source, for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore, open where the abscess is located and drain the pus, and do as you are able; and be careful not to cover the artery; and let some blood flow, so that the patient may die a natural death due to bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Then take remedies made from rue herb.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When any disease called "catarrh" occurs among the eyes or in a worse condition and the medicine does not help at all, then the last remedy is the cautery with which two arteries will be covered.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you wish to cover them, the patient should bend over his head; afterwards, rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then hold the patient's neck with one handkerchief; then look where the vein bites, and the places of both sides are behind the ears, and they are tied again; then mark the places with ink, then prick both with a sharp spatula of 2 parts until the wound comes up to the bone, and this should be through the wide part of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you wish, push the spatula under the artery and strike it from above, cutting as deep as two fingers through it.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is pricked, it should jump up without stopping repeatedly moving upward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open by itself, then you must measure the space of three fingers, then press and make incision up to the bone; and that which is required for blood to come out is 7 cubic centimeters, and sometimes a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the swelling of the artery; then observe the wound: if it remains above the bone without any pus coming out, then do not apply the hot poultice that you intended, instead hold the wound closed and heal it with ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	from emigration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old emigration and acute catarrh come, due to moisture in the tears and heat in the temples and ancient dementia and similar things, and it is treated by ways of medicine but none of it helps; if we open the arteries of the temples and cauterize them as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extraction [of what is stuck] is that the patient tilts his head back towards the hairs on his temples, and listens to the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well with its beating, and can be easily located except in some very cold people; and if it has been located, the patient tightens his neck with some cloth, then rubs the area with a rough fabric, and scratches the area with warm water until the artery becomes manifestly apparent; then take the spatula as shown here:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then gently score the skin until you see the artery, then pull it up towards the prongs, and carefully separate the threads on each side; and if the artery is delicate, turn it at the tip of the spatula, then press that part according to the size of the two shoulders. For if it is not pressed, it will not open easily in all places.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw the blood from the 5 cm to the 4th one; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it with a thick silk thread, which prevents pus from coming before the wound of the incision, and allows the flow of blood; then cut off the excess between the two threads in that hour itself, and if you see, cauterize it with the cautery knife up to the bone until the shoulders are severed; and this is the mutilating work, if the patient does not have a fever and he is of a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauteries are aid for curing the moisture; because it is of greater help to the moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, one should fill the area with old cotton and place well-made tourniquets on it; and when they are loosened, if it is cured with dry medicines that make pus, and with tourniquets, until it heals; and if without a cut of the artery as you work, hurry to cover it with cautery, or use vitriol and squeeze it with your hand so that the blood does not flow out; and if you do not have this, place your finger on the area until it becomes frozen, and moisten the area with cold water and squeeze it as needed; and those that are swollen and heavier in the extraction of the artery should be cauterized with this sharp cautery cutting .5 inches deep, but they should be thick for a longer time to preserve their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the strumens are too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two cuts, one being large in space; and when you have marked the two places, and you put hot iron on them until it reaches the bone, and pierce the vein in two places; and they should be separated by the two heads because it is not bonded with this cautery throughout; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	And the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are flowing into the veins that are on top of the head of the fire, and it does not help with any medicine that is applied there, and you see the patient writhing in pain, and feel the forehead trembling like a fever; and if they are weak and moist so that the hair of the scalp falls out, and the scalp becomes scorched from the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called the ancient one "contused cure", and it is that you make a cut at the back of the patient who has this disease in the hair he has on his forehead, then you make four cuts equally along the length of the forehead; and one of the cuts as two fingers all the way down the forehead from above to below, and the others two at the sides, through the eyebrows, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are at the sides through the eyebrows; and move your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be the size of three fingers joined together.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and a lot of linen rags to soak up the blood, then insert the pointed instrument (spatula) made of two parts as follows:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is through the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the skull that is between the two cuts down to the scalp, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then pull out this pointed instrument.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Push the instrument called "culter-like" into the first incision. It is very sharp from one side, but soft and not sharp from the other, and it has the shape of a:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And make the cutting edge face towards the skin, and the soft part facing the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle incision. And cut all the veins that run from the top of the eyes as long as the incision is continuous to where the opening of the skin begins, and then continue in the middle incision to the other side; and then remove equal amounts of blood, expressing the level for the blood taken; then put a tent of old cotton in each incision, and put over it damp linen soaked in wine and oil and ashes, and make sure no pus comes in; on the third day, loosen the ligament, and apply a large amount of fresh onion juice, then treat with ointment of basilicon with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyelids
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When anyone comes with an acute catarrh usually, and you see the eyes becoming swollen and small, and the vision blurred, and burned papers; and the hair falls out, and a headache occurs at pain ague, and the patient coughs; then recognize these symptoms that those matters and such catarrh do not come from any other place than many veins, and the medicine to cure it is that.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Then you instruct the patient to lean his back, then make a large cut in the front, and another deep one. (i.e., make an incision from the left temple to the right temple, and it should go up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; and when the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood with a sponge, and then press between the two sides of the cut and put old cotton, and linen strips; then cover it with dampened cloths soaked in wine and oil, and avoid hot abscess; when it is removed, you should rub the bone until char starts to form, then cure it with things that promote the growth of char.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice; administer it to these wounds to promote the growth of char everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppage of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains, animals, stones or similar items like iron; seeds, beans, peas; or flowing matter such as water and sand and similar substances.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	If a stone or other such thing falls into the ear and does not fit snugly in it nor grow inside it, place the affected ear near the sun. If you see the stone, apply some drops of purple oil or camphor oil, then provide extraction; have the patient cough to open the eardrum, and plug the ears with pieces of cloth or wool, and hold them above. Often, pus discharges through this treatment; and if it does not, provide extraction using fine tweezers as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out at the hinges, that's good; if not, introduce extraction with a thin hook of double curvature; and if it doesn't jump out by that means, make a wooden pin and push its head into the hole of the ear strongly, stop up that which is around the pin with soft wax so that the air cannot enter with the pin; then pull it out forcefully, for often it comes out in this way as we have said; and if it doesn't come out in this manner, take some glue from it and take the birds, and put any tool sharp for that purpose, and put a piece of cotton around; then press the glue on the stone or something else, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it doesn't jump out due to all the things that we have mentioned, hasten to make an incision in the ear so that pus and spasm come out; and the manner of the incision is such that you first lance the patient's head, drain the blood according to the measure of its power, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear upward, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fat or tissue dependent on it; and let the incision be like a crescent moon, until you reach the bone, then pull it out as much as possible, and suck the pus quickly to your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that swells, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer a thin, slender spatula in this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And make an incision in the grain, but do not do this if you think that the grain is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many cuts; then strain it with fine tweezers and water, as we have said, so that the extraction is clean.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	When water falls into the ear, instruct the patient to use ear drops made of warm vinegar and honey first, and to stuff the ear with cotton wool. Let it lie on that ear itself where the water is. If it jumps out due to this, that's good. If not, take several small, light pebbles according to the size of your finger, heat one slightly in the fire; then make the patient hold a stone or a piece of cotton wool in his ear, and press another pebble against it from the other side, and strike another pebble on the stone in the ear; keep doing this with stones hitting stones until all the water jumps out completely, and it should jump out entirely. If you see, take one more stick, and push one of the pebbles into the ear, and heat the other end of the stick until the smallest piece of wood is burning; then repeat this process with other sticks until all the water has jumped out as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of an animal, if it is small like a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is large and can be felt, perform extraction with tweezers. This is the easier thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and the treatment of distillations, and if the cure does not benefit, then you should look at the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, take them with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, take the string of which this form is given.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And make it narrow within and wide above. And insert the thinnest end into the ear according to the degree of pain of the patient, then pull the string completely; do this often until all the worms come out. If they do not obey to come out, stop the opening with cotton as I have said earlier; if the worms protrude not, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the removal of worms, and you will find them or treat the distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear to this apparatus, as you see in the given form:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.
