And make it narrow within and wide above with a silver or iron frame having one small hole, and over it a cover for the distillation; and to press inside the distillation, use one apparatus of iron well made for this purpose; and if you see that you need a scraper and wrap cotton around the tip, then put your oil or juice and any medicines in the string, which should be in the ear; then insert the scraper with all the cotton into the ear, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or the ear becomes warm; let the patient smell it within, and make sure the distillation is heated to about the same temperature as when it is distilled in the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicines will not be effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppage of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some deafness in the ears; and this same thing happens to men through stoppage of wounds or pus inside the ear, and this stoppage sometimes comes completely into the ear if it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a little hole showing the deafness, which can easily be seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, if the stoppage comes completely into the ear and cannot be seen, it is difficult to cure in many cases. In such case, you must put the sick person's ear in the sun and look inside. If you see a visible obstruction, you should open it with the spatula as shown here:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and piercing in front and behind entirely, so that it does not prick the ear; if the inflammation is of flesh or bone of the ear, then hold it with subtle tweezers and strike gently until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If the inflammation is within the ear, then take a subtle and gentle razor and heat it slightly in the fire, then place it against the side of the ear. If you feel the inflammation causing pain in the ear, pierce it gently, ensuring not to injure the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a lining according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a lining and moisten it in rosewater and powdered vitriol; if you see the ear swollen, then you must pull out the lining and insert another moistened linen made of rose oil and beeswax until the swelling is removed; then heal it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And when bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and linen in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other treatments to stop the bleeding which are either distilling methods.
de la char des papieres	of the charcoal from paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the method by which hairs that are damp and dry come from paper. It is necessary to stretch them with pliers and tweezers, and then rub their roots with a copper spatula. Then place it on broken glass.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if the hair cannot be removed by pulling, cauterize it with subtle lenticular cautery, and after incision is useful. Many times they repair, but nothing remains of their roots; and when the hairs are cauterized by fire, the roots burn and do not return.
de la gresle	Of the shingles
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Often in paper there come out things that resemble shingles both in form and hardness, and for this reason the disease is called "hail," and it is a collection of large moisture on the upper and lower sides of the paper; the treatment is as follows: wait until the hail becomes silent from all sides, which is an easy matter to know; then make an incision around it, then gently scrape each part, then take tweezers and remove it. If you cannot cover it without puncturing the paper slightly, do not worry the patient; and if the wound is large, join it with a suture and cure it until it heals; but if it is small, do not use force, for the ointments restore it soon and irritate the skin.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn over the paper, take tweezers and remove it, pressing from both sides; and if the paper is displaced by the incision, do not worry about it; and when the hail is removed, apply salty oil to the affected area and treat the wound with ointment until the patient recovers.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	This is grease that is infused in cloths of paper above, and this often happens with children rather than adults, and it causes great discomfort to their eyes, and they come down with catarrh at mornings, and cannot endure the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; and because of this they lie on their faces immediately, and sleep thereon, and their cloths are wet beneath their eyelids moistening the inflammation and the appearance that have been covered with the grease which opens in oil. And when you press the eye between your fingers and feel the grease between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of this procedure is that the patient places his head on your healthy one; then take one linen cloth and arrange a tent-like circle according to the quantity of grease from each part, then place it thereon; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the grease is gathered in the circle; then make a cut in the middle of the moisture using a sharp spatula making an incision no larger than the wound one makes in the vein opening; and cut through the skin until you see the grease; and in many cases, the grease comes out from the incision, according to the form of a white piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	1. Place a piece of thin, woven cloth between your fingers and turn your hand back and forth until it is spread out; make sure you do not stray in the incision, only to reach up to the marrow, and do not pierce it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the incision does not open at the beginning of the cut, slightly open it to make it appear; then spread it as we have said, soak cloths in water and oil, place them on the area, and hold bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there are such men who bite the oil and place it over to remove that moisture which is stuck. Then heal it until it is healed. And if an abscess hotly arises at the place, treat it with plasters soothing it until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	The hairs of the paper [or possibly: the hair on the paper]
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When the hairs grow on paper contrary to nature, and are nurtured, they cause harm to the eyes, and bring about types of diseases such as tears commonly associated with paper, softening of the paper and albugine, to the point of causing damage to the eyes; and there are four methods of treatment: either by cauterization using fire, or through medication ague according to what is described in the previous chapter on cauterization, and it is done either by incision and stitching, or by canes, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper with oil on your left hand; if it is converted (meaning if it curls around the oil), that is good; if not, you should poke an awl at each end of the paper where the hairs are growing out of the hairs; and remove one filament above the entire length of the paper, then shave the area beneath the paper where the hairs grow, entirely through the spatumile (possibly a kind of blunt knife or scalpel), from the large tear down to the small one; then pull out one filament, and place a small tent made of cotton and wool under the paper, then sew a figure of an incense thong (or possibly myrtle) on top of the paper, ensuring that the figure is proportionate to the amount of paper you wish to raise.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is a need to apply a large amount of papyrus as it has been softened; then spread the entire plaster on two lines that you have marked, starting from the large blister until the small one; and let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then push the cone into one of the two angles of the wound, then peel off all the skin; then bring the two edges together with a stitch of a needle and fine wool thread, squeeze out the blood, and make the excess threads adhere to the two scissors with any sticky substance, if you want to do this; and if not, have no cure for it, then leave the stitches and threads for two to four days; then treat the wound without stitching with dry and constricting things, as the papyrus revives at the wound's edge and holds it together, but the stitches are rotten (as the ancients say), and this is labor without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and in another way: and it is that you sign the papyrus with a figure like the thorn bush of myrtle, as we have counted, at four incisions opened according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply this equally over the small wounds according to the shape shown here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you cannot hold the pliers, and the object is not even, take a needle with one thread, and insert it through the figure; take another thread from the large notch, and the second thread from the small, and assemble the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift the skin as you have described, then sew together the two lips of the wound by stitching, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	Sometimes the hair of paper is converted: it is necessary to use what we have described for incision; but sewing in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of dogs is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and fold it according to what I said, and then make two cords by hand, and two thin threads equally long as the paper and the thickness of the spatula; take the two corners of the four pieces where the threads are; then assemble the one and the other subtly above the paper with oil, and bind the two cords from the four parts; leave it in this manner for several days, and the skin that is bound will die, rot and peel off, until it falls away.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes a long time, if you must apply force, then heal it until it is healed; and when the wound will be sutured, and the paper lifted, and the hairs will not grow anymore; and this is the shape of two dogs that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work (task) is such that you take a fine needle, and insert one thread of silk and fine; then assemble the dogs' heads closely and skillfully, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange another thin thread of silk briefly, and join the heads of the threads; then place the patient's head in your healthy state; expose it to the sun so that the work is visible, because this is a subtle and small work, then pierce the needle through the entire chase (hair) at the root of the hair adjacent, and let it penetrate quickly through the paper over the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the chase, and place the hair in the chase, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand so that the hairs come out from all the chase together with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will draw the chase down to the thread that you have arranged, until the chase comes out of the skin and can be seen by the oil's vision; then you will draw the chase and the thread, and let the oil and the patient rest for two or three days, until the hair roots and new flesh grows; and if the hairs are small, you should accompany one long natural hair with it, and let it grow along with that, until it is extended and then shave it.
de la porriture de l’oil	From the corruption of oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this illness, called "alecrati" or corruption comes in the oil, there are two ways it occurs: one natural and one unnatural. It happens suddenly due to a wound, an incision, or a cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the method of work in this case is to split that joint, separate its lips, and put linen tents inside it, and leave it until it heals; and you should not use anything in the treatment of it that dries and tightens. For if you do this, the illness returns worse than before; but you should work with things that soften, such as fenugreek; and the roasted linseed oil or linen seeds boiled and ground into any oil, and a linen tent should be wrapped around it, and treated with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you must take care so that it does not heal closed again in its former shape; and this work that we have said is only remedy for this disease, so that it does not return in its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	the pus that comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease called "axacrati", which is both natural and accidental. The accidents come from wounds and fissures and cauteries and similar things; and the way of the work in it is that you take an awl, where it has one double thread, and pierce it into the pus, and make it go from left to right eye, so that the threads come out at two cheeks of the pus; then put the charcoal on top of the awl, and apply a spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a rasp and place it in the slit, turn the paper, and make two slits where the costal cartilage lies within the paper; and let the corners of the two slits be at the angles of the incision you made, and let them form an angle such that when they are assembled, the figure will be like the figure of a letter with the name "Y Greek"; then remove that cartilage, according to its thickness where it underlies the paper, then join the two separated parts using a linen thread; then treat as we have said for the medicines softening and soothing, until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the illness comes from a slit or stitch or cautery, it is necessary that you make a deep incision under the hairs of the paper, as previously mentioned; then separate between the two leaves of a linen cloth, as I said; and the work should be done according to the shape of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and the wise masters prepare tools with all possible skill to bring the figure back to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for the work and the use of various instruments in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	quickly from the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture occurs in the hands of men in such a manner that the paper above is glued with white oil, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the point of a razor beneath the paper, and lift it up; hold it with pincers until you remove the substance that adheres to the spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too rough, so as not to cause pain to the patient due to a too sharp spatula injuring the oil; make your incision, from which you will scrape the assembled matter, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and heal the entire assembled matter, and sometimes in the sharp oil it becomes infected, and you lift up the sharp soft liquid and collyrium; then put between the paper and the oil a tent of linen, and put over the oil dampened wool in abundance from an egg; and after the third day use collyrium and other healing substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	the tip of the spatula
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Note that the nail has two forms: it is nerve-like and resembles a hard spike, and another which is not nerve-like but resembles white solidified moisture when touched with iron and cooked in pincers, and neither begin near the great eyelid, but gradually grow to cover the entire eye and light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient places their head in your hand, then you pull out the hairs; next take paper with your hand, then bend the nail into tweezers of small double curvature and hold it above; then take a needle, put a horse hair or cow or ox hair and a strong thread on it, bend the tip of the needle slightly and pierce the nail, and pass the needle through completely, tie the nail with the thread and hold it above, remove all the hair from the side of the nail where there is skin and silk at the root to the head, then crush the remaining part in the root of the armpit with all subtle spatumile and small forces, leaving the natural flesh or armpit so that blood does not come out of the armpit as usual; and sometimes the nail is only placed on the incision and at the thread, as we have said; then remove all the spatumile from the place as described here:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And ensure that the spatumile does not touch the flesh and tear it, and that the vein is not pierced; then after the incision pour oil a little bit of broken fat and make a poultice from litharge, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous and you cannot push the needle through it, and the uncines cannot enter it, this condition of the nail is often treated with medicine; and as I have mentioned in the division, when you see it covered, then open the oil of the patient and take a little sharp spatumile according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently scrape the nail above, and if you see that it does not diminish at all and the reason persists, then distill from your mouth into the collyrium oil made of litharge and red collyrium powder, and instill the oil until the next day; then perform the same work again according to this same procedure, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the oil, as with an abscess, then let it lactate, and first treat the abscess hot until it is healed, then perform the same work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the wound harms the oil greatly, suspend it in onion juice and cut a small portion of it, so that tears do not come out; then distill red collyrium oil made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	Of the flesh which grows upon the eyeball
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	There are times when a red flesh grows over the eyeball of some men, covering it and turning it towards the outside and resembling a rosebud from a balustrade; and the operation is such that the patient places his head on the couch, then opens the eyes, and all that skin surrounding it should be cut with scissors accordingly, and it must be kept tight; then cut the first layer of skin, and continue cutting to the end with the razor, and be careful not to wound the oil gland at the operation; and let the incision be made with a spatula as described in the operation of the nail and with small forces like those used to remove the septum, according to the form shown after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is completed and all the skin is removed, use oil of egg white or you crush it where you distill red colloid and resemble corrosive medicines, and place on top the oil facing outward cotton with chicken egg yolk, so that it is assured that the abscess remains hot; and if something remains there, and the wound becomes covered, and you doubt that the abscess remains hot, leave the oil and treat the abscess with cooling remedies for hot abscesses; then return to your operation until it heals, and do this for each skin layer that is treated with oil in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But in every case it is necessary that you ease the treatment of each weak part along the natural way; and regarding the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not strike your hand into any of these works until you see that this member can endure that work.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	These are red eyes covered by oil and take their work in sight and weaken the eye all day. Therefore, it is necessary first to check if the oil, where the sebel is, is outside and has no other disease but the sebel; then proceed as follows: Instruct the patient to put his head on your healthy side, then hold these eyes still for a long time according to your wisdom, and make the compresses subtle and double according to this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And the organs should be two times in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then these veins should be gently squeezed subtly, and the blood sucked out hour by hour until you see the veins swell outside of the oil; and ensure that you do not prick the oil with the points of the spathulas, and perform this task at midday before the sun, and be very warm during your work so as not to overheat the veins; and when you have done this, if it distills green and red oil colicers to correct those that remain clogged.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect everything in that hour, make a plaster on the oil of soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is alleviated and the abscess is sure to heal, then continue as before in this manner until it is healthy; and this is the form of treatment:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mirroring fistula is called "arissati": when you cure it with cautery and burning medicine as I have previously said, and it is not healed, there is a trick in it that you open above the abscess, where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, you should cover it with all the instruments mentioned here; it is called "rough head," and should be made of iron as shown in the following figure:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the bone that is corrupt, then turn it between your hands, and press your hand slightly until you know that the corruption is restored; do this once, then restore the bone with medicinal force.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joint is sutured, and pus forms there, and the body of the bone is sutured, and remains like that for 40 days, and it does not swell or abscess, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healthy; if this is not the case, then there is no other remedy but to return the fistula to the hollow of the thigh according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with medicinal hot things, and when it is uncovered, take one awl according to this form, and let the head of the awl be at four angles, and the shaft be tapered until the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone near the socket, and move your hand away from the oil by about one finger's breadth, then turn the awl all the way until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it if they hold their hand over their thigh; and then restore the joint with dry medicine as I have shown you, and when pus forms and hardens the joint, the matter goes to the thigh; it is an easier thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the flow of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are wide open throughout the entire body and there is no disturbance in the ship, nor any diminishment, you must restrain the patient; then clean it, apply poultices or hot irons to help heal, then put oil on .i. link made of cedarwood and aloe and incense and saffron, and then hold the oil tight, and bandage it with cloths and linen; and the manner of the linens is that you take soft linens, fold each one in four, and then place one on top of another according to the quantity that the eyes require; then hold them together with a strong bandage, and renew the poultices to help heal without cutting; then remove the poultices and leave the oil tight for day and night, and if the link dissolves, you must tighten it strongly; then remove the link after the day and night, and if you see the oil healing, that is good; if not, repeat the bandage, the linens, the link and the poultices until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	From the rupture of a rotten cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the watery eye and open, and they bring forth paper-like matter, as small as a grain of resin, and it is frightening to see; then, if you cover it, the remedy is such that you insert an awl into the root of the part underneath until the one above, then insert another awl with double thread from the corner of the wound; and make it perforate, leave the first awl according to its position; then hold the eye of the double-threaded filament and wrap a part of the eye around it, and tighten it well, then remove the awl and put soft wool soaked in oil on top of it; and leave it until the filaments grow with the eye, then cure the oil with comforting substances until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is held closed by the eye on each side of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes become large in appearance, pierce them with a fine spatula that comes from oil, and correct the moisture albujine, and then remove it; then leave it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the oil bowl
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not far from being an abscess assembled in the eye, resembling an acute swelling, but it is not an acute one; and the appearance of its operation is such that you make the patient sit on a chair prepared and upright. Then take the head with both hands, move it as much as you see the abscess coming to your eyes; then pierce it, and do not drain and uncover the light, and let the patient observe the things as he used to; and if it does not drain, know that it is an acute one, and if the draining of the abscess is not prepared as we have said. Seat the patient between your hands, then take the subtle spatumile and poke through the corneal cloth .1 inch along the continuation of the conjunctive with the cornea and the corona, until the abscess issues; and when it has issued, distill in the hot, thick oil mixed with honey, or acute or fenugreek boiled with honey, then cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	the acute oils
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the appearance of acute oils in their division, and what is necessary for piercing; if you operate according to health. You should place the patient between your hands, away from light due to the sun, and press the healthy oil and tighten it very firmly; then take a piece of paper of the oil with your left hand if the hairs are on the left side, or with your right hand if the hairs are on the right side; then take in your right hand (left hand) the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand (right hand), if the hairs are on the other side; then put the point of the instrument through the cornea at a distance of one finger's width, along the lower blenchore of the oil, to the minor eyelid part; then push the "almagda" instrument firmly, and press your hand as much as it pierces in the blenchore of the oil, and feel that the "almagda" comes to the void place; and the measure of the way "almagda" should be at the full length of the space from the eyelid to the end of the black line; and this is the cornea of the oil; you will see the bone in the paper due to the clarity of the corneal cloth, and then put the instrument as far as the place where the acute is, then press it down a little more. If the acute drains now, let the patient observe in front of him and the instrument in his oil.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, if the second vein rises again, place the force with the instrument, and when it is pierced and does not rise further, press it gently around your hand little by little; then put in a little bit of gemmed oil on top, and let it drain out from within. Then put oil soaked linen or cloth in rose oil and egg abundantly, and seal with the oil. In our time, and those of our era, we put common powder with an abundance of egg on top.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the oil cannot enter due to its hardness, as there are some people who have excessively hard hairs; in such cases, you must take the instrument called "alberit", which is shaped like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then pierce only the conjunctiva without going too deep, but make a shallow incision first, then insert oil, as we have said; and when the task is completed, arrange for the patient to sleep on his back in a dark room for seven leagues; be careful of all movements, take light foods, and do not move his head either to the right or left, and bind him according to his position until the third day; then unbind him in the same dark room, examine his sight, show him some things, and then rebind him for a week; it is not advisable to do this during the treatment time or after the incision is made, but rather to alleviate it because the oil rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If an abscess swells up, you should lance the oil before the seventh day, and direct the one who soothes an abscess; and when it is soothed, you should close the eye and place a linen cloth over it for a day or two, and remain in that dark house. Then leave the house little by little, and convert to your rooms; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country everyone was subjected to almagda piercing, so that the water comes out, but I never saw anyone in our land, nor did I read it in any ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And here are the resemblances of the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them will see them; and they are from arain properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the head of oxen of this same subtlety, and the rear end in four corners should be sharp.
de la char sor le neis	of the cartilage on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes nasal cartilages are born or grow in various ways, causing some to resemble scorpions with many legs; and there may be some whose cartilage is swollen in dark color, and others of good bone color. Therefore, for those cartilages that are swollen but not inflamed, you must have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, and pour warm water onto these cartilages, then pull them out; afterwards, grasp what you can hold with a fine sharp spatula on one side until you know that the cartilage is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing uncovered that cannot be covered, open it all with sharp and thin instruments, so nothing remains; and if the abscess is not closed, apply the remedy as necessary; and if the abscesses are malignant, hasten and cauterize until the pus is drained and all the charred matter is removed, then cover or dress it with oil or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If there is no discharge of pus and moisture reaches the palace (the head), it indicates that it is healthy; but if moisture does not perforate as necessary, it means that charred matter has formed in the bone above, so instruments do not work to cut: then you should insert a large flax thread into the nostril up to the power of your hand, and pull it out smelling the pus coming from inside the nose; and have children at school perform this many times, and it is an easy thing for him who wishes to do it; then hold one head with one hand that comes through the nostril, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and know which one follows the other by us who are present near the flax thread. Perform this until you know that the flax thread has rotted the charred matter; then remove the flax thread, drain the blood, wet the flax in Egyptian ointment, and replace it back to the nostril as before; perform this for 4 days or more, until the ointment corrodes everything that is remaining of the charred matter; and then apply a linen cloth to the nose for several days until it is healthy, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, as it is said when distilling oils and medicines through the nostrils.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or brass, resembling a covered lamp, as a pipe, and lead it thus; and if you see, make a closed pipe, and the instruments full for purging the head; and have one handle on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	About the skin over the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" appears on the forehead of the nose and grows larger and larger until it is visible to see; therefore, you must cut it at the beginning and completely excise it, then put the cautery or burning medicine over it; and if you delay covering it until it becomes large, take care if it is hard, dark in color, with poor sensitivity: do not touch it with iron because it is an enlarged abscess, for when it is touched even once, it causes great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is soft touching, not hard in color, and you can cover it completely, have the patient empty their bowels and cautiously cut it, then cure the area with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a dislocation of continuation comes in one of these cartilages, it is not much use except in some men. Therefore, if such an event occurs in any, you should examine whether the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then sew together the two lips (of the joint) with stitches, then heal it until it heals completely; and if the lips have already been disconnected from one side and the other, you must cut all the areas where they are torn apart as much as they smell, then reconnect the two lips with stitches and tighten them, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood powder on top, and incense pulverized; and place a piece of plaster of strong or another plaster that adheres on top of the powders, and let it remain until it solidifies by itself, then heal it with ointment until it heals completely.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is that you assemble the dislocation: either by needles, as we have said in the abdomen stitching; or by thread, as I told you earlier.
des apostemes des levres	of the lips (of a wound)
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the hands of men, an abscess hard within the lips occurs, resembling grains of various sizes; then you must turn the lips and make a cut above each one, take it with the forceps and crush it in every part; afterwards use vitriol powder on the wound until the pus is drained; and then apply alum to heal the wound with dry things until it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	from the jawbone
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often a swelling arises on the jawbone, which the ancients called "albulus"; you must hold it with the forceps and crush its root, allowing the blood to flow out; then apply vitriol powder or other drying powders to the wound; if the swelling returns after the incision and this happens repeatedly, you must crush it again and cauterize it; but it does not return after cauterization. These are the shapes of instruments for covering.
des sordens	Of sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are sores gathered at the root of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, rough and harsh scabs that are ugly; and sometimes the teeth turn black and greenish, as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; it is necessary that you make the patient sit with your hands, and his head in your lap, and clean the teeth or scabs exposed, until nothing remains; and do this for blackness and greenness, and for yellowish and other spots, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is there at the first instance, that is good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, as long as you have everything cleaned; and know that the teeth need different types of instruments to clean them, according to what the work shows, because the one who cleans the teeth has different shapes than the one who cleans between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you cure the tooth of its pain, it is necessary that you draw slowly as much as possible, for this must not be done quickly; because it is a very high substance up to where there is no excuse to shave.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore, when the patient is constrained to draw a tooth, it is necessary that you are certain of the diseased tooth. Many times, despite the pain the patient feels, they may believe it is a healthy tooth and pull out the good one; however, the pain does not disappear until the diseased tooth has been removed, as we have observed with many saints; and when you are certain of the diseased tooth, you should incise around the tooth all the way. Use a strong spatula to protect the gum from all sides; then move it with your fingers or subtle pliers at the very base and base of the tooth, until it is well loosened; then firmly hold the pliers; and keep the patient's head in your saint between your knees, so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After the tooth is drawn out correctly and it does not come out easily, take any of these instruments and push gently from each side, and move it as you did before. If the root is pierced and eaten away, you must fill it with bandages where the holes are; then hold it subtly with pliers so that it does not break while being pulled; and it must be done very carefully around the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be aware that you do not break it, and leave a part behind, and return the tooth to the patient due to the malice of the root causing greater pain than before. Be careful that you do not do as the ignorant saints sometimes do, who with their haste and recklessness break the chariot (the tooth), and do not bring what we have mentioned; but they sometimes cause great disease through the roots that remain or because of the broken chariot, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is drawn, wash the area with wine or oil and soap; and if bleeding comes out, apply vitriol powder; if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, which mute the teeth first, should be long pointed and have thick handles, not bending when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And have large handles so they do not bend when pulling, made of good iron, and toothed for holding on.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains at the opening, you must place cotton wool moistened in butter on it for 1 to 2 days until the wound is softened, then insert the forceps called "algefri", making the head seem like a beak; and within them make it as smooth as a file, this is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	If the roots do not come out with all these forceps, you must uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", namely tweezers, of which this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be large and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with these, that's good; if not, help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps himself with this instrument which has two prongs, this is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other iron instruments that are in front for the reasons of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pliers, here is its shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be strong so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and similarly, other instruments, which are not counted here; and the wise masters discover their own instrument by themselves, according to what their work and the disease indicate, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach an instrument due to diversity among them, and if it breaks the cart or any other bone, or it could be used, then search for the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and help with movements, here is its shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and strong to hold the bone, so it does not slip, but can be held and removed; then restore the joint with medicines suitable for this, and if there is purulence in the bone, and it is small, use this instrument entirely:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear not according to natural form, and the shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, if you know that the teeth are not aligned after the tooth, and it is not in the correct position, and cannot be straightened or filed: then use a rasp; and if there is an abscess with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is like a small beak, and sharp at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is similarly like the file from which one makes the needles; and in the file, the tooth little by little gnaws at hand for many light hours, so that it does not move until it chisels through; then the flat part at the end must be smoothed with any sharpener, and if the tip is too sharp and it bites the tongue, it is necessary to file down the sharpness so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.
