Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth loosen, whether from impact or falling out, and the patient cannot press down on that which they eat without spitting, and you have tried to cure them with constricting medicines, but it is of no use; then you must restrain them with a gold wire, for silver wires become green and rot, but gold does not change; and the wire should be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are moving, take the wire and tie it double between the healthy teeth, then place the diseased teeth in between them, if there is one or more, as long as you can do so skillfully up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then start covering again until you reach the part where you started, and hold your hand skillfully and firmly, so that it does not move; and hold your position at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then grip the diseased teeth with the wire in pliers, assemble them, and reposition them, placing them in such a way that they do not bite the tongue; and then leave them as tight as they can stay, and if they loosen or the wires break, you must restrain it with another wire; if it remains and serves for some time, it is the form of the tooth and the figure of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two diseased teeth, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, if you replace it in its place, freshly, as we have said; and do not interfere unless the person is wise and patient. Sometimes one makes the shape of an ox's tooth, and replaces it where it lacks, and holds it in place as we have said, and let it stay for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes the ligament under the tongue comes from nature itself or due to accidental injury; and the treatments are as follows: open the mouth of the patient, hold their head steady, lift the tongue, then cover the nervous ligament with a wide piece of material, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if it feels hard or not, and this is due to sudden injury, insert an ointment and cover it widely; ensure that the cut is not too deep, as there is an artery beneath it. After you have done this, raise the tongue with rose water or warm water, then put a linen tent over it; let the patient bite it every night so the wound can heal. If discharge of blood occurs, apply vitriol powder; and if the wound does not heal, cauterize it with slow-burning cautery which is good for this purpose, then treat it with another treatment until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a swelling of various colors, whether black or hard, such that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a boil; and if it is descending towards whiteness and there is moisture, throw the onion on it, and let a thin spatula be placed beneath it and release it from both sides; and if it resists your work, put vitriol powder on it until it is burned, then return to your work as long as you draw out all the pus; then remove the pus and serum, and cure it with other cures until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	swellings of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes there come within the throat swellings called "godath," and they are properly called the two almonds. When you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of small size and light color, do not touch it with iron. If it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, for the reason of bleeding; but leave it until it becomes soft, and then you will cut it open or it will burst by itself; if it is white in color and the root is thin, prepare the instrument to cover it, but first make sure that the abscess is calm and quiet. Then have the patient sit before the sun, and his head should be on your hand, and open his mouth and take the sergeant between his hands, and press the tongue down onto the entire instrument, as shown here; it is made of silver or thin brass, like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue with this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the onion and thrust it into the abscess, and pull it upwards as far as you can; and pull out any foreign matter from there, afterwards strike with the instrument, in which form it appears similar to a hammer; and yet the head is bent, and one part is against another, and they are very sharp, and made of iron or bronze:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument, strike it with the pliers, in which form it appears similar to:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have the instrument, strike one of the abscesses, and then strike the other in the same manner; after making an incision, gargarize the patient with hot, sharp, and mild water, and when bleeding occurs, gargarize the patient with hot, or scorched pomegranate seeds, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then let it heal until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses than the two appear in the throat, if they do, strike them accordingly as the two equal.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I will treat a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, to be precise, a small abscess; and it had grown very close all over the throat, so the woman could not exhale due to the blocked passage, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if it lasted for a day or two. The abscess had swollen so much that it had filled about two pouches through the two openings of the throat. Then I immediately lanced it once, then pulled out a large piece of pus; afterwards I opened another hole in the other opening of the throat, and I opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I lanced the abscess again, took a part of it, and only a little blood came out; thus the passage from the throat was unblocked for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting away at that abscess for a long time; the abscess grew again and filled the space I had created, until it became very large; then I trapped it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus the growth of the abscess was stopped; and I left those parts, and nothing more happened to them except that God did something with them afterwards.
de l’uve	I will treat a woman with an eye problem that was inside her eyeball, in other words, an inflammation of the eyelid; and it had grown very close all over the eyelid, so the woman could not open her eyes due to the swelling, and she could neither see nor blink, and would have gone blind if it lasted for a day or two. The inflammation had swollen so much that it had filled about two pouches inside the eyeball. Then I immediately lanced it once, then pulled out a large piece of pus; afterwards I opened another hole in the other side of the eyelid, and I held her eyelids open and pressed them against each other; after that, I lanced the inflammation again, took a part of it, and only a little blood came out; thus the growth of the inflammation was stopped for the woman, and she began to see again. The inflammation grew again and filled the space I had created, until it became very large; then I trapped it and cauterized it inside her eyeball: thus the growth of the inflammation was stopped; and I left those parts, and nothing more happened to them except that God did something with them afterwards.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the eye swelling is long and narrow, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thick and round, it is called "eye". When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not work, and you see that the large abscesses are subsiding, and it becomes subtle, you must cut it; and the one that is rounded and not long; and it is red or purple or black, you must make an incision of it. For there is great danger with the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to the way I have said, in terms of its thickness and length, you should make the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument we have mentioned earlier; then lance the abscess in the eye, pull it out, and cut it at one or two of the intervals that I have said in the incision of the almonds. And you must not cut more than the superfluidity that is beyond the natural limit; for if you do, it causes pain to the voice and speech; and after the lancing, use what we have said in the incision of the almonds, and let it heal until it is healed. And if the patient fears the cutting, you must use an instrument for cauterization to ease his fear. The method of cauterization is hot and sharp. It is that the patient puts his head in your lap, and then you press his tongue against the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and hold it with a hot, sharp object, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and use the handle of this instrument, as shown here:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the head of a hair or medication is put on a head, as the comb of a spoon, and the instrument is placed entirely over the medicine above the eye; and the patient lies on his side, so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine, but not down the throat, and the blood; then hold your hand over the entire medicine and press it onto the eye for about half an hour until you see it swell and the bites of the medicine are appeased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument all over the cotton in the canal above, until the cotton sticks to the eye; and do this repeatedly, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and lie for four or five days. And if you have to start the cautery again with the medicine, renew it, and after the cautery, wash around the eye with cotton wrapped in butter, clean what is around the medicine; and irrigate with cold water, and heal with gargarisms until it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective than incision, not only cautery; if it is healed by fumigation according to this method, take camomile, yarrow, rue, and wormwood, and assemble them all or some of these in one pot, and put them inside, and boil it; the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot have one comb-like instrument as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it should be made of silver or lead, and one of the heads should be inserted into the mouth of the patient until the vapors rise to the eye through the canal, until the eye is killed; afterwards renew it repeatedly, until the eye dries, and make sure you do not perform this at the beginning of an abscess boil, because many things may happen; and do not do this unless in the declination of an abscess boil. And if this instrument is not present, take a canal and place inside the patient's head a hen's feather eggshell, so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot; because the hen's eggshell will not let the vapor burden the mouth, and it is good cure along with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often it happens that a bone or fish spine enters the throat, or something similar; in such cases, you must pull out what you can see and press the tongue against the sun with all instruments so that you can see it move; and if it does not open by itself and is swallowed back into the throat, make the patient vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will be expelled through vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, a piece of cotton, a root of lettuce, or a small piece of dry bread; tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will stick, and then you pull it out; and if it does not come out as described above, take a plank-like instrument in this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the top so that it can enter the throat more easily, and hold the head up high; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, or the patient will choke, do not push the bone deeper; it is better for the patient to push the instrument, because it can move or the object is expelled; if they push it downward, you pull it out equally with the instrument until it is expelled.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the saliva from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	At times, the saliva of the patient is used as medicine, as I've mentioned in the division, by means of medicines. And when it does not help at all, then look into the throat of the patient towards the sun, since you press his tongue with the instrument I have told you about. If you see saliva, draw it out with a small spoon or fine tweezers suitable for that purpose. If these are not available, use a hair-rope, put it in the patient's throat, then push or lift the end of the rope with a hot iron and do this frequently. And keep the patient wet all day long. Then take a full ounce of cold water, open his mouth, pour it in so he can swallow, move it with your hand often; and as soon as the saliva feels the water, it will drop out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	If it does not drop out as we have said, fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the instrument I have told you about in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will certainly come out. The manner of fumigation is that you take a pot that has charcoal and cover it with a perforated cloth, and place the tip of the instrument inside; then pour your fumigation into it, and make the patient hold the head of the cane in his mouth, and close his mouth so that no smoke escapes, but comes only to the saliva; and the saliva will now certainly come out, and if it does not drop out, repeat the fumigation many times; let the patient endure thirst, eat salted foods and almonds, and drink no water; then it will be necessary that it goes out through this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the wound, appears, when it can be seen, resembles curved tweezers for entering into the throat; and it has the appearance of a syringe beak, and it should have roughness of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	Chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Abscesses have many similarities, according to what is recalled in the following sections of this book from one and another, and they are different in perforation and incision; and there are two ways in which the first way resembles it because it contains moisture. And the second way is in joints or at organs. Indeed, abscesses on the head are different than those on the base, and abscesses around a bone are different than those that come up at joints, and each should have its judgment in treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if there are abscesses which should not be pierced until the bubble is ripe according to its completion; and if there are such abscesses that it is necessary to pierce them when they are hard, and do not die according to their ripening, like abscesses located near joints. For when abscesses arise near joints, and it is left until it is burst, possibly the ligament and nerve of the joint will become corrupted, which causes contraction in that member. Or if the abscess is located at the principal part, and you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal part; or if it is located at the base, if pierced before it is ripe, it will not be possible to pierce it fully, and it will become tunneled inside, and a fistula will form, and will not heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time for perforating the abscess which is ripe according to its completion, and it is when the pain is alleviated, and the disappearance of the fever, and the decrease of the pain and redness, and the swelling and subsiding of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should make the perforation sit lower than the abscess, and where it has started to open; and the perforation should be as long as the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal or without a covering.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In the places that swell, according to that member. And when abscesses are in fleshy areas, it is better to leave the perforation until it is confirmed in digestion completion, as we have said. For if you pierce it beforehand, the body will fill with much pus; and possibly harden the edges and the inside of it. And for any abscess that is pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the member requires. And it should be necessary to bring small abscesses, small perforations; and large abscesses, large perforations, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses where the care is required, and covered; when it has become as thin as a cloth, and softened, it should be treated like the babies: and for those that are cut into four angles, and for those whose cover is like the myrtle leaf, as abscesses from the joints; and for such abscesses where a round cut is made, and other cuts and similar covering.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	One who has no head, such as an abscess superficial, it is necessary that you pierce it fully; and when the abscess is large and it contains a great bulge, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out some of it; stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw nothing incorrectly; do this many times with care, as much as the pus subsides; meanwhile if the patient is weak, or a woman, or small children, or old men weakened, be careful for sometimes the pus escapes suddenly with the death of the patient, and you will not be at fault. Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, clean the wound, and check if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is wide open, bring linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess and there is much damage, it is necessary that you stuff in every one a linen bandage so that they meet each other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and you have shaved around it, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or raw linen without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and cure it with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If bleeding occurs in your work, bring cold water and ash, wet a cloth and place it on the place repeatedly. And if the bleeding persists, provide treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter, and the limbs or abscesses are very nervous, it is necessary that you put hot towels and cloths moistened with wine and oil on them; and if it is summer, and the limbs are fatty, it is necessary that you place cold towels moistened with water and oil, or cold water and oil, until the third day, as we have said; then remove the abscess and clean and treat it as necessary, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses; now I have told you how to proceed with the treatments of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	The sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	For the small abscesses that come on the head, there are methods known to us, similar to poultices, such as a linseed bag and many others. Some have fat and moisture like pustules; and some are hard and stony at the base and there is no doubt whether the arteries interfere. And the treatment of the abdomen is that you prove it with all instruments called "entromissoire", from which the following form comes, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, they do it above the long way. And when the moisture is emptied, scrape skin without leaving any hair that contains that moisture, for it returns immediately when one leaves anything; then put cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; otherwise in water and oil, and apply it to the wound and leave it until the next day; and those who are delayed by night will come back. And renew the cotton the second and third day, as before, until you know that it does not remain by night; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healthy. And if the abscess contains one knot of fat, cut according to this form, long; and throw your onions there, and scrape it from all sides, and apply all your care to draw out the purulence where it lies; and if the arteries interfere with you, do as I told you before. And do the same for the abscess if it is hard and stony, and treat and heal as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the treatment for a hard and moist abscess is easier because it has little blood. And if any of these abscesses or head have no moisture, and one of those I cut where an old woman's head was, I found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break; and if one had pierced it with anything, it would have made as deep a wound as from a stone. In other abscesses coming from the head or elsewhere, they should be opened all day long depending on the location, to let pus out; and treat them as necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Often this abscess occurs at the neck, under the chin, and in armpits, and sometimes it appears elsewhere on the body, and they are swollen and connected to each other. And each scrofula is properly within its own cavity, as we have said of the lymph node and the abscess of the head; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many. There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that are malignant and do not want to obey health. In such a case when you see it in good condition for treatment, and it resembles the color of the body, and it is silent on all sides and is neither near the nerves of the neck nor the artery nor the conduit, and is not deep; then you should cut it above, remove the skin from each part, and place two fingers of the cautery at the opening, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and pull gently and carefully, making sure that you do not cover the nerve or vein, and do not use too sharp a lancet or cutter, so that the hand does not slip, and look ahead so that you do not cover what should not be covered.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not stop bleeding, put vitriol powder or some powders that stop blood into the wound, and press the wound; leave it until the abscess is soothed and the wound becomes soft and starts to pus. When the pus is stopped, return to your work; then check if there are any small scrofulas remaining near the root of the scrofula, cut and clean them. If there is a large one at the root of the scrofula, do not cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall out through the thread, without causing harm; then dress the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you treat the entire scrofula (boil), you must gather the two lips of the wound and sew them together, as there is no room for excess due to the large size of the scrofula. You should cover the root and draw out the pus, and sew it as we have said. For those scrofulas with excess, pierce where it has been closed; and pierce it as described above, depending on its location, then introduce tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is clean, cure it with ointment made from sweet-smelling char.
de squinance	And for strangury (a difficult or painful urination), you must crush barley grain in wine and give it to drink, and add the juice of dried figs; this will ease the pain and make urination easier.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the size of the throat; however, I have never seen one do it in our land, and it is written in their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinch, the incision of the throat called "epiglote" should be made; and no aid should be given by them, because all the veins and the opening of the sickness are in those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two almond-sized places.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the mouth, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to avoid the danger of strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Then, when we want to cut the epiglote, it is necessary that we cut it below four circles or two small cuts across, between the circles or through the thickness of the siphac, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And if the loins are to be cut open for the incision of the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is afraid, then you must stretch the skin of the throat in its entire length, then split the cartilage as far as it reaches to the trachea; and sever the vessels of blood if you see anything, and then cauterize the wound, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the incision of the trachea which passes through the broken place, and by the lack of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed during which doubt exists about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound with care, and close it entirely without damaging the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote healing until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi says one should not do this until the throat is completely stopped up and the patient has been judged dead and his spirit departed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then tie the epiglottis for this reason, because the patient cannot breathe properly and breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And therefore the ancients command to leave the wound open until the malice of the sickness has passed, and it has passed in 3 days or 4.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they command to sew up the wound and heal, until it is healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a maiden took one knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the windpipe.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called to heal it, but found it lifeless.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found blood flowing from it, but I realized that neither voice nor conduit could be heard or followed except through the throat, and the veins flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I quickly sewed up the wound and cured it until it was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And it did not happen to the maiden that her voice became hoarse, and she returned afterwards to her condition.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore I say that in the swelling of the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	From the large throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "throat hernia", and it is a large abscess of a yellowish color, and it is common in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And it is according to two ways: natural and accidental; where the natural has no instrument.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two ways, where one is similar to fatness in us, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from us due to arteries.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear, and one should not perform strong actions on anyone who is small; it must be proven and searched through the entire opening.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it as hard as a knot and it cannot be opened in any way, strike it like one strikes the nose, and pull it all the way off if there is any of it left.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And bind it well, and heal it as necessary, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of the nose
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways to perform a nose surgery exist, which I will describe one by one.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now I must explain all the difference between dislocation and fracture.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Dislocation is characterized by heat and fever lasting until the swelling has passed, then the fracture is complete, after which the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With a fracture, there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains one sack, which is its own sac and is the same color as the body, and begins like an abscess, and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they can be of two types: fat or moist, and they are often the same colors as I have mentioned in the classification.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the cure of the knot, that you test and inquire first about every instrument which is called "entromissoire", according to what its form will come or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of the inquiry of abscesses by us is that you take or the more moist place that you find in the abscess and turn your fingers little by little, until you feel that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then draw the instrument called "entromissoire", and take care that it does not break.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs out of the wound, make it color as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the incision no moisture comes out, know that it is fat, then make a cross-shaped incision, take hold of it with pincers, gently scrape off from both sides and watch the cloth or bandage you pull through it to ensure it comes out healthy with the knot;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot pull it out whole, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	If there remains nothing, it returns many times to the nose.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it persists a little and does not bother you, apply some corrosive powder to the wound, hold the wound closed, put warm soothing things on the abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it heals.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it is large, make two lips of the wound, and treat it with a remedy that stops bleeding.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is beating against you or something else, rush and use vitriol powder instead, let it lie for 2 to 4 days until the wound heals, and allow the boil of blood to rest; then return to cover what was left uncovered with linen.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the probing instruments, and there are three types: large, medium, and small; and if it has four squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three types: large, medium, and small, to surround abscesses with fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are similar to the needles used to sew charms, made of citron cane, iron, or silver. The yellow ones are more valuable for surrounding the boils with fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the ulcers resemble each other, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are ulcers with two curves in four ways too.   \*The text seems to be referring to the types and number of ulcers, but it is unclear what the "two curves" might refer to without further context.\*
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and if there are ulcers with four curves, they also have four kinds; and if there are ulcers with two curves, or ulcers with only one curve, and all of them are in their place.   \*The text seems to be referring to the types and number of ulcers, but it is unclear what the "two curves" and "four curves" might refer to without further context.\*
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these [things] which are cut open is sharp, and of those who do not cut all the way through except from one side, where scourging of the nerves takes place, because the vein or nerve should not be struck.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these incisions [or openings], the skin is tied together in bands so that the patient does not hurt himself at the opening of abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	And they are of four kinds: large, small, and medium-sized, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And it is not used anywhere other than in charnu (charred) limbs, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar joints.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling fists' scourges, in this shape, to draw blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed sometimes at the place that heals from veins and arteries, and sometimes it is returned in this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	At times, the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, until they seem like breasts of a woman;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, it is necessary to be according to this form of the following line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then remove the fat, apply medicine to the wound with healing herbs, then sew together the two lips of the wound to heal it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast leans downwards and is flattened due to its size like women, cut it into two pieces along similar cuts;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	From this, one should keep the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this form, from this line 'b' up to line 'g'.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then peel the skin that is between the two lips (of an arrow wound), remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment, until it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed or the incision is not completely made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And leave it to consume what remains of meat and fat, then heal it when it is clean.
des apostemes des asselles	from the abscess on the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are treated as hard scrofulas with swellings that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those containing moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire hole that is in the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment as needed until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, make incisions as we have said in the treatment of scrofula, and if the wound forms a hole, bring fire as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	from the cutting of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery is ruptured, and the skin that is above it becomes sutured, there are often abscesses, and the same happens to an opened vein and abscess.

et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to the swelling of the vein, then you must smear this with your hand the entire skin from the abscess.   --> and if the abscess arises from a swollen vein, then you should smear this over the whole skin from the abscess using your hand.

des apostemes des ners	abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, abscesses of the nerves occur when they are injured or from excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this often occurs in shoulders and thumbs, and in all places where there are joints, that is to say, severe abscesses, and its color resembles the body's color, and it is found in many conditions causing pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is being straightened, the patient feels pain, and it is not completely within the body, but under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And it should be completely closed on all sides, and not go forward or backward, nor up or down, and the one in the joints should not be covered with iron, for perhaps it would contract.

des grosses boces pendans	Hanging large swellings
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	There is often in bellies and nowhere else the disease called "fungus," which resembles warts, and has subtle roots and large heads; some of them are small and others are very large.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor. si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart. quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil bursts
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterization of a wound or a cut in the scrotum, as happens in other places, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries as described earlier, or from swelling;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from the incision of the scrotum and the emergence of the boil, its appearance resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing with little pain, and opens in various ways.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	and if it is from the intestine, then it is more varied, and when it is pressed with the fingers, it sinks back in, and then returns, and sometimes it becomes hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and through great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, it is an easy matter and opens easily when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and they are pierced according to a certain quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to windiness, it yields easily with pressure, and the work appears when you look at it whether it is from the blood of the artery or vein or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	You must leave the treatment. For there is doubt and fear as I told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and vein.

dou chancre	of the sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of a sore and how to treat it with medicines and when to use iron cure; now let us say what a sore is like in marriage, and great caution should be taken in its treatment, and the ancients said that when sores are in places where they can be shaved like sores that occur in mammary glands and thighs, and similar places, it must be completely removed when it begins; but when it is large and old, one should not approach it, for I have never seen anyone heal it; no one has ever healed it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when they are in place and can be removed as we have said, it is that you purge the patient once of black bile; then make him purge if he has obvious fullness, then prepare the patient. That is, shave the area where the operation will take place; then pour boiling oil or other hot substance over the wound, and let all pus flow out; leave no bone or cartilage unbroken; and let all blood flow freely. And press well on the area with your hand or something else, and if the discharge of blood opposes the incision of an artery or a vein, cauterize it until the wound is closed; then heal it with other treatment until it heals.
de ydropisie	of the hydropieric disease
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have previously explained the signs of hydropiery and the methods by which the water is made, and the symptoms of each form, as well as the treatment using medicine and iron. These are only revealed in two forms of hydropiery - tympanites and hypoarch, for they are fatal. Therefore, when treating this form of hydropiery known as "eclites" with medicine, and if the treatment does not help, one should consider whether the patient is weak or has other diseases such as a solution of the stomach and similar things. In such cases, iron should not be used because there is doubt. If you see a strong patient who only has hydropiery and no other disease, then proceed as follows:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lift the patient upright on your hands, and the minister presses the belly from below, directing the liquid to the lowest part of the buttocks. Then take the pointed spinal probe according to this shape: It should be pierced through two parts and not so deep that it reaches the intestine when inserted, nor should it blunt.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then check if the urine is directed towards the intestines: If it is directed due to liver disease, the incision should be on the left side of the belly two fingers' width; and if it is due to constipation, it should be on the right, and the patient must not lie on the incision so that superfluous fluids do not run to that weak place.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce the skin with the tool and push it, then put your hand between the skin and the bladder as when peeling an apple to the thickness of a nail or more. Then pierce the bladder until the instrument comes to the watery place, which is the bladder, then draw it out and put this tool of the form shown here: It resembles a thin silver chain, made from lead or light iron, and has one small hole on the underside; it has three holes on one side, two on another, and one on another; and the bladder is shaped like a quill, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes carve the pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	On the head above is the anus, so that when the instrument comes to the water, now push it up on the instrument; empty then either half or a third part, for if you empty more than necessary in that hour, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit due to the weapon, or he will faint, or he will come close to death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to the amount of its power, and according to what the dispositions of the power mean in the patient and his pulse; then pull out the instrument and hold the water, and it is now held back for the caution that stops the bleeding which is above the siphon, as I have spoken about, so you pierce as follows; then restart the instrument the next day if you see the patient suffering from this, and draw out a small amount of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.
