Do this every day, and be careful not to let it stay too long but only a little water. And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave much water, cure him with burial or hot sand, and by sweating or bathing and in the sun, and anoint with wine; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	A child is sometimes born without foreskin or the foreskin is small and not in its proper place. If this needs to be addressed immediately, it should be pierced with a very thin spatula as follows: then place a fine silken cloth on the foreskin and hold it and keep it for 2 to 4 days until urine can be produced, at which point the cloth should be removed and urination allowed; and if necessary, it should be replaced, as the urine that comes out does not close it.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the foreskin is small, it may be treated with a piece of silk cloth as mentioned earlier, which will allow it to expand. Those who do not have the foreskin in its proper place are blistered, for no one is born with the foreskin at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before raising their penis; and they cannot enjoy sexual intercourse because the matter cannot reach the opening, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of work is that the patient lies supine on his back, with the head of the penis and the buttocks at the same level, so that the testicle falls into the scrotum as required; and guard against excessive bleeding that often occurs, and if it happens, stop the bleeding from the wound, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the penis ulcers
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often this albathe appears on the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly sores; and there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; you must pick them up once a week with a thin instrument, cut and clean them all, then put cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on top; then treat it with diaphinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the elbow is unhealthy, of a putrid color and swollen, it is necessary that you apply cautery. When you have applied it, and if the elbow is inside the arm, with some part within the flesh and some part protruding, it is necessary that you remove the elbow which is within first; and when it is sewn up, cure it externally. For when you treat it together, the joints of the arm are not secure, and blackness and corruption come into the arm and the elbow joint; it is necessary to clean everything that is black and corrupted, then place it on a plaster made of honey and flour which is made from the rind of pumpkin seeds and apply other treatments until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this form: The cauterization should have two dispositions together: for the bleeding, and for corruption; and if the joint of the arm is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you bore a channel in the arm with a plank, and make the patient urinate; and when the hairs are separated at the tip of the arm which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, or occurs due to an injury or abscess, then it is necessary to shave it with one instrument, until the ligaments are disconnected, and the joint of the arm is released from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is a painful thing to speak of this, you should make an incision with a lancet about half an inch deep along the vein and the skin; then pierce carefully between two fingers, and place one thin linen cloth soaked in cold water on it immediately.
de la circoncision	of circumcision (when referring to the surgical procedure)
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not without reason and similar to other wounds; however, when we perform this work by our will and specifically on infants, it is necessary that we do the best work and the easiest for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children, for they did not practice it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted most of the masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around one day and all at once; however, there were those who feared it because there are two layers, and by chance if one above is cut, the one below may remain.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the coping is covered, and the pain is doubled; and at the circumcision of the tip of the member, it is not certain that the point of the tool touches the member; and by chance, the iron may slip during the circumcision of the nail, and ruin the work, and many times they are born without need for circumcision, and I have wanted this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the amputation which is made at the joint of the limb I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut equally well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	When you press your hand, it cuts equally throughout the entire thickness; but that the thread be well tightened around the skin; and should the method of the first operation be that you make the child think that you do not tie the thread around him except for the rod only, and then let him go in all ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then you make him be between your hands straight, and place the forces (tools) between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the rod and blow or say a word, and draw it up until the head of the rod is in; then clean it well of the filth that has assembled there, then tie the ligature signet with a double thread, then tie the other end to another ligament; hold the second ligature at the knuckle and at the index finger, and cut between the two ligaments, then pull the cord quickly and draw the tip of the rod.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the blood coagulate point by point, for it is clotted; and put powder on top and on the powder place a piece of cloth glued with a spoonful of cooked egg white steeped in rosewater, mixed with fresh rose oil; and leave it until the next day, and treat it with another treatment until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces for healing is as follows: the two shoulders should be tender and should be cut, and they should also be as large as the fist equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of healing is when the flesh within is cut open; therefore, it must be stretched with the nail, so that the joint becomes abscessed; and equalize it, and if you cannot hold it with the nail, use pliers, and then equalize it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they exceed three days, and that which is beneath the worm [abscess] is swollen, let it be left until the abscess subsides, and gently lance it; if it bursts as you can move it, do not injure the part of the worm, this will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure the place with powder, as we have said treating powders, and if it bursts excessively, and goes above, it will not harm; so cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from obstruction by a stone, or blood congealed, or pus, or frozen water, or similar things, as we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not expelled, and you see it is retained due to the stone in the bladder or neck of the bladder, then the patient must be bent over his knees; his feet should be placed on a table or support, and he should extend his abdomen from the upper part of his back, and hold the patient as firmly as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is forced to express the stone above it, so that the urine is expelled.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instruments called "syringe," of which this is the form: it should be made of thin, light silver head, like a bird's feather; and its cane should be one and a half palms long, and fine at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the method of the urine discharge is as follows: you take one double thread, tie one end to the head, be it of linen or cotton, and push the head into the syringe with the thread inside; then gather the excess of the linen and push it up to the head of the syringe, then oil or butter the syringe and place the patient on a seat, and anoint the bladder and penis with moist oil, olive oil, and warm water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the base of the penis, then bend the penis upward towards the scrotum; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and have the patient feel it coming until it empties completely, which is not done according to this order for any other reason than that the guide leading where it goes is twisted; then draw the thread all along the linen piece by piece, and the urine follows the linen, then pull the thread fiercely, and correct the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Illness of the bladder (or urinary system)
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	For scorchings or blood coming into the bladder (or urinary system), or pus is gathered there, and you see it distill acids and medicines, do all the instruments that are called "clepsydra" (hydrotherapy device). The shape is:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and if it is three punctures: two from one side and one from the other, as you can see; and the medicine should flow through the channel so that it stops the penis well without addition, if one can draw out the moisture, and push when necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you see throwing your medicines into the bladder, place the head of the goat in the moisture, and draw it through with what is within; if you pull the moisture out of the goat, and then push forcefully on what was within; the moisture will enter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient can feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the form of the subtle enema for cleansing the bladder; it is as follows:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	It is made of silver or copper, and the head is higher. Underneath it are one hand or the link. Then take a sheep bladder and put the moisture that you want to enema the bladder with inside. Next, sew it between two hands using good double thread, and heat one end of the moisturizer over the fire. Then insert the tip of the enema into the vagina, then hold your hand on top of the bladder, until the patient feels that the moisturizer has entered the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment and make one circle, pierce it roundly around; then put a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one would assemble a thimble, and place inside it what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, press it with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of stones
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division of stones the methods and extraction along with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone implanted in the rain and all the signs, and in what stone one should operate according to size; and in the bladder, and in the vein; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder resembling water in its subtlety; it opens a passage, enlarges the patient's urine channel, and pierces it many times, then ties it up; and many foundations occur because of these jumps; and children's healing is light until they are four years old, and it is very severe in the elderly, and it is in the middle, for those who are between youth and old age; and the treatment is lighter for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, first it is necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines. For it sometimes hinders seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet and tilt them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes moves upwards; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands should be under his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declining downwards; then press and touch it with your hand.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the abdomen, act quickly and cut into it now. And if it does not fall to the touch of everything, moisten your left index finger with oil, if the patient is a child or an unfinished young person; dip it in its foundation, seek the stone, and when you find it at your finger, pierce the kidney; then press down on it and push it towards where you intend to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the assistant to press the kidney with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then put the spatula covering it, so that it forms:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make an incision between the testicles and the foundation, not in the middle but along the left side of the navel; and it should be straight above the stone, and your fingers should be close to or on the foundation, and the incision should be wide across, and thin within, according to the size of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance, if the pressure is applied which is at its base, it should leap without any effort; know that there is a stone or angles and margins there; if it is grated (or ground), if it is soft like a plum and round, then it will issue out easily.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	Then in the place where there are angles and margins, make a larger incision; if it does not leap, then you must strain on top with pliers like a liming tool at its head to force the stone out without escaping; or push a subtle curved instrument under the stone at its head; and if you cannot trick it in this way, widen .1 inch and remove the cortex; if it does not come out, strain it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there are more than one stone, push the largest one into the bladder first, then hit it, then draw it out, and the smaller ones after if there are more. If it is very large, it must be broken, and a larger incision must be made. For the patient, two things can happen: either he dies or urine comes out immediately where the lees cannot seal; but nevertheless, make an effort to draw or break with pliers as much as you can until it is drawn out in pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it closed, then place a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and cold rosewater and cool water on top, to ease the abscess heat; afterwards, make the patient rest on his neck, and do not undo the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you undo it (the bandage), wash well the wound with oil and water, then apply the ointment of defyfinicon and the ointment of basilicon until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if an abscess with erosion comes on the wound and blood clots in the bladder, and it is retained in this way without urinating, then you must press your thumb on the wound, and drain the blood, for if it remains, it will cause the bladder to corrode and perforate.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then clean the wound that is wet and dirty and full of pus, and help in all ways you know while it is healthy; and it is necessary to bind both legs and place the medicine on the site.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	If the stone is small and it is conducted along the urine and stuck in, and urine cannot come out; cure it as I say hereafter, cut it multiple times, and excuse yourself from the cutting because of this treatment. I have already proven this thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod according to this form and with four angles pierced in one thorn:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft of the stone inside the bladder, so that it cannot return to the bladder; then push the awl lightly into the shaft; and turn the awl little by little in the stone, until you can pierce the stone from another side; soon the urine will come out, then press your hand on what is stuck inside the stone which is within the shaft. Soon it will be broken, and flee with the urine, and the patient will be healed;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie a thread around the stone and another one above, then drive the shaft towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the first thread, and clean the congealed blood from the wound; heal it until it heals.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone from women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens rarely that a stone enters a woman, and if it ever occurs, the cure is severe, and it is forbidden for four reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well how to examine herself, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a woman skilled in this art with hands; and the fourth way is that the stone within the woman is deeper than the stone in a man, so it requires a more profound incision, causing great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if you must resort to this, you should take a skilled midwife, and if one is difficult to find, do not hesitate to have a chaste maiden of subtle understanding; and present her to a wise bailiff or a woman who knows a part of the art, and order her to perform whatever you command regarding the incision of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And examine well if the woman is a virgin: then her husband must enter her door or foundation and seek the stone; and if he finds it, he should press it under his door, and recommend that she push her door with the sickness, and hold and press her left hand on her bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If he finds it, then she should push it gently from the bladder to the root of the thigh until it reaches the root of the groin; then strike on the stone at the root of the thigh near the cervix, where it is most movable, and feel the stone in that area; and do not move her hand above or below the stone, and make a small cut at the first sign of movement.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then push the root towards the loins, if you feel the stone, make an incision in the wound so that the stone can come out, and know that there are many types of stones: small or large, rough or smooth, long or round, and with ridges. Know their appearances to recognize their outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the bone protrudes, place vitriol powder on it and keep it for an hour until the bone is set; then return to your work, as long as the stone remains hard, and have tools that I told you for the extraction of the stone in men to assist you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If the bone protrudes and it is an artery that is cut, place powder on the area and bind it with straps and bandages, do not attempt to move it again, and leave the stone alone and do not draw it out, as there is a risk the patient may die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the wounds have closed, return to your work, as long as the stone remains hard.
de hernie carnouse	Of carnous hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquose is not something other than an accumulation of moisture or white pus, which is beneath the bladder, containing the egg; and it is called "white pus", and sometimes it is properly within the egg's membrane, if one thinks it is another egg; and this is the skin of the bladder between the white pus that we have said, and this does not occur unless there is a rupture.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this accumulation is due to weakness that comes from the bladder, and this matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from impact on the bladder, and this moisture can have various colors: either it becomes darkening to yellow, or it is without red, black, white, or watery white, and this happens more often.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white and soft as we have said, then it is an abscess, i.e., a long pouch like the shape of an egg, and its opening does not appear, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the very fabric [of the abscess], then it is an abscess with part of the egg-like shape, and for this reason, one thinks that it is another [type of] abscess.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the egg-like shape and the white soft part, one can feel it well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, probe it all around carefully, so that the form [of the abscess] may be as described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, the one who comes after the incision judges what is inside.

puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the bladder completely full of water at one large opening, and drain all the water, and then place your fingers, and stretch the bladder upwards; do not touch the core of the kidneys, but only the bladder; cut through everything or in pieces the side of it carefully, for if you do not cut it well, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the egg jumps out of your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the bladder work; then join the two layers of the kidney core with a stitch, and treat it as you would other wounds until it heals.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted with some other disease, you must tie the vessels that are suspended, taking care of the discharge of blood; then cut the kidney and remove the bladder, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the wound has gathered pus in two parts, know that these are the branches; if you cut the other part similarly, then suck out the blood, and put moistened linen in oil on it.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put linen moistened in wine and oil on it, and place two coins on top, and cover with double cloth, and tie it all up with a rope in this shape:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths made of coarse linen in this shape and sew them together to form a band around the thigh, placing one coin on its base up to the back, and the other at the handle part. The remaining ends should be gathered into the buckle of the garter.

de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the cheek
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the treatment of this condition, there is fear in various positions, which makes it seem to me that one should move [the patient];

Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, many abscesses come from the body, especially in the bowels; and this happens often.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is due to excessive sourness or heat that spreads in the bowels, or from injury;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and it does not find pain, and it is a painful abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And possibly it is a painful and hard abscess, and sometimes it comes from an artery, or from inflammation of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from an artery, it can be known by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	And it is not necessary to touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	A person who is afflicted by swelling of the vein can be recognized by their disposition to express the touch of the fingers.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can make the cut on this appearance, and on other sores;

et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is a boil on the face, or in that which is within the cavities, you should release all the pus and let it heal.

de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the cheeks

de la routure dou syfac	of the dislocation of the thigh

de hernie carnouse	of soft hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy, I never saw anyone dare to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made like a graft that connects the bone, in this manner you bind the vessels, after cutting them lightly below.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then fill it in and treat the abscess of those who work on it, until the vessels bleed; and heal it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes gangrene comes in wounds, as we have said, and open the veins; and do not remove any intestines from the bowels, and if some are removed, it is bad, and repair them every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	And if it remains too long at this point, the wound or pus gathers, as the intestines discharge.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	This happens by the spreading of the pus (abscess), which is harmful, as we have said, because it is spread, then it becomes soft and swollen, and the sores open up.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this way:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and the patient lies on his back on a flat surface between your hands, then strike the swollen area with an iron rod of about three finger-widths wide;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	And then draw out the pus that is under the skin, afterwards take the rod and place it on the apparent place of the abscess;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press to the bottom of the stomach, then cut two apparent places on the sides of the abscess above the rod's head, and make one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the rod's head, and do not cover it with anything or stretch or extend the abscess or any other thing, as I told you in the treatment of intestinal worms.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then heal it with wound treatment. And when you bandage the wounds, if they fester and infect the wound, keep treating it until it heals.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The siphon is constricted, without any appearance in the opening, and the cauteries are moved closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin on the cheeks
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin on the cheeks becomes soft in some men, because the charms that are inside are softened and it is visible; and it is necessary, when one sees it needs to be cured, to make the patient lie on their back, and to cut the softened skin on top of the natural skin; then bring the two lips together at a stitch, and if you see, sew first the excess skin that has been softened at 2 or 4 strong stitches; then cut between the stitches, and the wound is cured as other wounds, until it heals, and sew the thread.
dou chastrement	the punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	It is mentioned that chastisement is discussed in our law, and I would rather not speak of it in this book, as it is not necessary for the purpose at hand. There are two reasons: one is when the mirrors in the law respond to questions about it and its cure; the other, because we often need chastisement of animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, pigs, and others. Therefore, I say that chastisement is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting. In the way we perform it by attraction, we sit the animal in hot water until its genitals are softened; then we grasp them with our hand, keeping them pressed until they are put back and you no longer feel them.
des hermofrodites	hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	1. Hermaphroditism is according to .ij. (two) kinds in humans: the first kind is when there are two openings apert as in the figure of nature of a woman, where it has hair, and sometimes urine appears from within them. And the second kind is in women, who have something above the penis as a rod and two openings. The treatment of a man and a woman is that you cut around the adjacent parts (or genitals), and treat them like other wounds; in the second kind, however, for men whose urine squirts through the skin of the openings, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	the treatment
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	tentigene is a growth on the natural part, which is too ugly to see; and some women have it as big as a hand, and this is its treatment. You should remove the excess of the growth with your hand or scissors, and lightly cut it; do not go too deep so that bleeding does not occur, then cure it with other remedies until it heals. For another growth that arises from the husband's mouth, and leaks, and sometimes squirts out, and is like a cow, and for this reason, it was called by the ancients "cow disease." You should cut it off as described above, and cure it until it heals.
de erratique	Of a dislocation
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	The dislocation occurs when the birth canal is not perceived or too narrow, and it is either natural by birth or accidental due to illness; or it is caused by a twisted presentation, or by a subtle or large fistula, and it happens in the marriage chamber, on the side, or under it, regardless of where it is. It should be avoided, and the conception, childbirth, and flowers should be prevented from occurring. Recognition of these conditions is through the observation of the belly. If the swelling appears near the hands or at the right side, then do this: place your two index fingers together, and the woman should lie on her back with her legs spread; then form the two fingers, so that the subtle fistula remains round, and the swelling is reduced; then take wool, wet it in oil, and put it on the area. Let the woman rest at home each day, so that it cannot heal. If the fistula is hard and large, you must cut it with a spatumile resembling a mirte leaf. If the swelling is of flesh born, suspend it to the onyx and cut; have ready the medicines for stopping bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, all mixed with much egg; then bring a wide plank, so that the wound cannot heal; and in this way let it be long, and bring a tent of dry linen; then cure other wounds until it is healed. And when in childbirth there comes flesh born, it should be covered in this manner, unless the abscess is enlarged. For in an enlarged abscess in childbirth, one should not touch to heal.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. "Emorroydes are openings of veins that often do not heal without cauterization, and when emorroides become old they turn into thrombosis; and we have said in the division what their similarities are, and the signs, and I will say here those which receive cure."
des apostemes de la marris	"of the anus abscesses"
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses come in the anus, such as carbuncles, pierced abscesses, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and other illnesses that I have mentioned in the division. Therefore, it is necessary that I speak here about the carbuncle abscess which comes in the anus, which is not the same as those that collect pus; and if you want to know the work of iron, look to see if the carbuncle abscess is acute at the beginning of its occurrence, and full of heat and fever, and becomes red when touched. Do not rush to pierce it, but let it heal until the pain subsides; then make the patient lie on one seat, and have two small seats or he can lean on them, and support his back and bend his legs towards the opposite side of the leg; spread his thighs, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a strong rope; then suck out the pus from the affected side, and bring the instrument used to open the anus opening. The form follows as described here: it is necessary that when you introduce this instrument, that you pierce the rectum first to know the depth of the anus, so that the instrument does not enter too deeply or burn the patient; if the instrument is larger, cover the depth of the anus with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt it; and cover the top, and mark the instrument. When the abscess opens, and one massages it by hand, it must be covered with a clean bandage, or lint; and when the carbuncle is empty, put dry rose oil or green oil-soaked cloths on the wound, and place the cloth from the wound at the opening of the anus, and over the anus and the handle, place a clean, moistened cloth soaked in vinegar or cooked malves; then apply ointment after two days, until it heals; and sometimes lift the anus and the wound with an enema of vinegar and honey, and then of cooked lys roots and aristolochia longa. Then return to the ointment. If the wound is healing in the anus, it is necessary that you avoid burning with iron, but treat it as we have mentioned in the division.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	The midwife must first recognize the figure of natural childbirth and its signs when she sees the woman pushing downward and desiring to urinate; then hasten the birth of the infant; for when it descends towards the head, the second one follows with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press the woman's abdomen so that the infant comes out quickly; for when it rises towards the head, the afterbirth is expelled by the husband with his waste through good cleansing; and this which comes in another way does not come naturally. For sometimes it comes on its feet, or the body or thighs, or hands, or on the abdomen, or backside, and is turned accidentally onto its neck, and by other evil figures; it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skillful in these matters, and to avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the figures as to how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes down naturally towards its head and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and the vital forces of the infant are weak, make her sit on a saddle or have women hold her; and anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then insert the small spatula (spatumile) between her fingers as shown in the figure:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And split the second bone, and strike it with its claw so that the moisture which is within escapes; and press the woman's abdomen until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must fumigate the woman with musk-scented fenugreek oil; afterwards make her take and vomit emetics, and hold her mouth and nose closed for an hour; this will now cause the child to be born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the birth of the child upon its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child is born on its feet, then you must push it upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn [the limb] slowly and slowly, until it is even.
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take one piece of cloth and stretch it slowly and slowly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Can it jump up to the knees, if commanded, and make it vomit with condyssium (a type of medication);
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps up (it means the wound or lesion), God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, turn it little by little until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Thus it should be done gently.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come as we have said, take mastic resin of high quality, oil of roses, and melted gum arabic, and grind everything in one mortar.
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and place the mixture on the nature of the woman from within and outside this ointment.
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	Make him sit in acute pain beneath his ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when it is softened below [the affected area], make one cupping glass of myrrh, place it on top, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	Then make him sit on a chair, then make him vomit and hold his mouth and nose closed, and press lightly on the stomach, because the infant is now struggling;
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the birth of the child on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When an infant comes in this form, place the bale (balister) with your hands slowly.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	Then hold it on its neck, and let the feet hang downwards, and lay it on one bed.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	Fold your hands slowly, then take hold of its hands above the stomach, and push its buttocks downwards until it is ready to be delivered.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	If the infant does not come out by itself, take its feet and gently pull it straight, then push on its stomach, and your hands will follow.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	And rock the child gently, little by little; command the woman to take care until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the emergence of the child which comes out one hand wide
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to manipulate the hand [to deliver it].
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	If you cannot manipulate [the baby], raise the woman and walk around.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If it cannot walk, lay it on a bed or a flat surface, and bend its legs.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the musk-like substance I have mentioned;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if it does not give birth, lay it on a chair or seat, then try to bring back the hand.
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and deliver the child according to its natural shape, make it vomit, and tell her to take hold of it until the afterbirth issues forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	The issue of the child on its neck, and it has spread out its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	You must hold the child's hand firmly, then turn it gradually and gently rotate it.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	And when it is equalized, place it on a high muslin cloth and oil, as we have said, then instruct it to move gradually.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	And when you have done this, make it sit on a chair and instruct it to take hold of itself; then make it vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same manner, treat everything else.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to be in this manner for everything, press the dislocation with your finger, until the moisture is expelled.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	And if the child pushes up against its face and neck, press it from the back so that it is not held, and the child dies.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	Then push the child inside until you have placed it as required, and command the woman to take care of herself once.
adonques si istra legierement.	Therefore, ease it gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	From the birth of twins   (or from twin pregnancy)
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is known that twins are born often and sometimes three or four; and this is not strange and rarely happens.   (It is common for twins to be born, but it is rare for more than two to be born at once.)
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	It is a strange thing, and if they are named, they do not live.   (It is a rare occurrence that twins are named and survive.)
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they [the symptoms] multiply, and are desired by the one who inflicts them, who is tied to evil.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And sometimes they occur naturally like teeth under the gums, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they emerge violently, the treatment is as we have said, and let the bailiff be skilled, and do quickly and easily whatever it does.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and perform it in such a way that it contributes to healing.
de plusors enfans	Of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes they are formed in marriage (i.e. one, two, three, four, five, six, seven or more, up to fifteen), and all are fully formed like a child by the measurement of the sagacious Glorious One (God),
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	And it is necessary that the bailiff knows all this, for sometimes similar things happen;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Carry out as required.
de l’enfant mort	Of a dead child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When treating the woman with a dead child or miscarriage, as I have said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are forced to work by hand;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	It is necessary to know if the woman is of sound virtue, and not have any accident or fear of death.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	The woman should be laid on her back, with her head lowered, and her legs raised.
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	The minister shall shave her from the waist down, or tie her to the bed so that she is not treated in the delivery of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	Then rub the mouth of the midwife with moist oils mixed with musk and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint her hands with these oils and these musks.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	Then push it gently into the socket, then seek one level where it can fit.
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and beware if the entrails are protruding that they should draw them back onto their head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if he inserts the tendons into his eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under his beard or near the joints or near the ribs,
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	And if the dislocation is on limbs, pierce or press them gently towards the middle.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	And you should hold the limb with your right hand and place the flat part between your left-hand fingers, and push it all the way with your entire hand gently, and pierce the limb in one of the places mentioned until it reaches the empty state.
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the limb:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then pierce towards another bone, where needed, so that the dislocations are equal;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	And then it should be straightened equally by moving from one side to the other, in order for movement to occur, and the bones should be brought together tightly to hold them as shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	If there remains a part, then the physician should apply oil to one of his fingers and push it into that part, and pull the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if there remains no part, then place this bone or higher up and do so until it goes completely out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot return due to strain,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	then you should wrap it in a cloth, until it goes away;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	Then cut the tendon at the base of the joint or at the palm, and you must do the same in the other hand, and with both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's hips are wide and they are narrow at birth, or if there is a sharp head assembled,
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	It is necessary that you insert the pointed sponge between your fingers, and bend the head and extract the pus.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	you should take it to the instrument called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the tools or chapter that follows this one.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and in the same way make the child naturally born with a large head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then cut the bones with the pincers.
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	And if the shoulder jumps out and is held by force, it should be cut open, as far as the moisture that has come out or gone deeper;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	If it cannot be pushed back in, then break it into parts where you can.
