et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	And they corrupt much matter, and it becomes a fistula, and much pus comes out that all flow and moisture from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	And they put many cures around it for two years, but there was no healer in the art of hands.
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I was called to him, and I saw his leg and the medicines that they were treating it with.
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and the one who walked with great swelling of the body due to pus.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And the bodies of the young ones become red, and they have a yellowish tint.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I pitched a tent in one of these wounds, then I searched for all the wounds,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	And I found that he was coming towards another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I then hastened, and made an incision in one of the boils until I uncovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it rotten and pierced, and the rot came up to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was the one who appeared to be the rotten bone, and thought that there was no other rot except what I left;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to heal the wound with salves for a long time, but could not suture (it).
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	And then examine (or inspect) and discover the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found the continuous corruption in the bone, and burned it out, and then left it open, and then tried to mend the joint;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not as I covered around a palm of the bone, and drove it back in entirely;
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I returned it to medicines; and it healed and mended quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it is not necessary to continue the work except due to the feebleness of the patient who could not endure,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For the blood evacuation occurred often, but he was completely healthy.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and a hard cyst grew on the bone, and he had a good constitution and did not have any harm or damage in all things, nor to his air or coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated as follows:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take one splint, and bind it to the open end of the broken bone,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	instruct anyone not to extend it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	And place another thread of linen larger than the first thread, and tie it above the skin that is over the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	Extend the head (the affected area), so that you pull out the corrupt flesh beneath.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the skin on the place where you wish to be, so that the skin does not prick the flesh.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a splint or a board under the bone to cover the corrupt flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And it is necessary to see and feel the corruption as much as possible, and also to examine it again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	If the bone is corrupt, but does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	If you expose the whole flesh; then put one splint under it,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	If the corruption is found in one part of the bone and is long enough for a thumb (one inch),
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is at the joint, strike the corrupted joint, and be the bone or part it contains on the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption extends through two joints, there is no other remedy than to cover (it).
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if the corruption is at the hand or foot, it is a very serious matter.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	However, you must investigate this corruption, how it arises.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	And clean it in every way you can, but do not harm the vein or nerve.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the saw and files for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And for each kind of work, it is necessary to prepare the instrument accordingly.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	And know that the work will show you the instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the symptoms of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you think about the instrument that is needed, according to what is required.
dou feu	hot fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The heads can burst from within, or from outside.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have applied this corrosive medicine through the treatment of medicines, and it does not help at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	it is necessary to cover that limb up to the level where the corrosion occurs,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	If the patient is scorched by this [cautery], he shall let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and if the signs are that the member becomes black, as though it were burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards it turns black, then goes this corruption of the member to member.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	And take hold of the entire body; hasten to cover it.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	If it is due to the sting of some venomous animals such as a sea scorpion or viper and similar creatures,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the corruption is at the top of the tooth, strike it and do not give it room to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches up to the hand, strike at the joint, so that corruption does not reach up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it reaches past the elbow, strike at the bone; if it passes the bone, it is death,
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no foreign remedy of value but the quantity of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And thus do as when corruption comes or pain: if it comes at the first joint, then crush it after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	If it comes with pain, then crush everything in pain;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	If it ascends to the leg, then crush at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	If it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but letting the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	And the manner of covering or dressing the limb is such that you bind it above and below.
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	Extend one minister to the lower ligament, and another minister to the upper ligament.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And you should cut open the flesh that is between the two ligaments with a spoon-shaped instrument, wide enough to expose the bone.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	Then dress or cover it (the exposed bone), and place one linen cloth on each side, to ensure that the dressing does not touch healthy skin.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And another injury and abscess comes to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	If bleeding occurs when you work, then cauterize the area immediately.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	Then place some restraining powders on it; return to your medicine until it is completed,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then tie the limb with a convenient ligature, and heal it until it is sound.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	And I will tell you what happened to one man in a pit:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	a man fell into a pit where there was darkness that seemed to be on fire:
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	the corrosion came first in his mouth from the pit, until it had filled the whole pit;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the body sees corruption, it pierces copper with its (the body's) lance, and becomes healthy.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards the corruption or pain returns from the hand, and it came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I placed remedies that were repelling after the cleansing of the body, but the corruption could not cease.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and you command me to bandage the hand, but I do not want, as I had hope to repel the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	And he also fears if I cut his hand, that he will die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the virtue of the man was weak; and he gave up all hope, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and struck his hand with a copper sword, and recovered.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not told this story for any other reason than to show what should be done if it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	An abscess sometimes comes in a charred place and remains for so long that it causes a great accumulation of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then they run and pierce, and the pus jumps out, and the place remains open like a wound of a warrior.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above it becomes as thin as one layer of unspun linen cloth.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they will not go down to the bone or nerve, and such a disease is called "sain".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And it is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it reaches the bone in full, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	The cook should be such that you cover the entire hide, and also when it is thin, like a cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not leave it because of its rotting.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have a suspicion that the flesh hardens, and the corruption is not complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the flesh becomes thick, treat it with clysterism (enema) in this way:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	examine if the breasts are large, and the swelling within them is foul-smelling,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Then give him an Egyptian enema made in this way:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take asafetida, oil, and litharge equally, and cook them together in one vessel over fire.
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take from it according to your need, and make it into water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and apply it as a poultice on the breast, and press the wound;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	And leave the medication on for two hours, then draw it out while pulling on it;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this several times until the breast is healed and the pus is discharged;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	And once is cleansed with ashes water;
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, take vine ash and pour water over it,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	Then bleed, and in ointmenting (applying an ointment), as long as you know that the breast is well healed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear it, or Egyptian medicine (?) nor the ash of embers,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if the ointmenting (ointment) has water and honey or a little litharge powdered;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	Or you will anoint it with honey and sweet wine, where the honey has properties to cleanse and wash.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	And the wine will heal the wound.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	Then, when you have done this and are sure that the wound is clean,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the anointing causes pus to form in them,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And you take plaster of definition, make it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	You anoint it with some medicines and ointments, of which I have mentioned the properties for treating sores.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	if the sore on the breast is small, and the bandage cannot enter it,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if it is a wound from a small spear and you put on it an Egyptian ointment in a tent.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And the ointment of basilicon, as it is diluted;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, leave it at least one fingerbreadth or a clisterium can enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound that pours out blood is on top, press or lower it to where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the wound is deep, do not allow anything to fill it with flesh.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot cover the chest below as you see,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then prepare everything in such a manner that the belly protrudes as much as it can towards the lowest level.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	because when the belly is full, do not leave any room for a hernia to occur.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the chest below as you see,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	If it appears in this manner: that the arm moves slightly downwards, without letting anything from the arm.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take medicines to strengthen for placing on the breast.
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and stretch over one linen cloth that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then hold the pressure towards the wound on the breast, a bit larger than the first.
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	The wound is to be anointed with oil or another cloth according to the quantity of the injury,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the injured breast to align the bone, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and he who is on the injured breast, removes often to remove the bone,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know that it runs from the bone, whether it is poisoned or infected, or digested, or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	And take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	And when your medicine has been applied in this manner and you see the nature that rises above the sore on the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	If you know that the breast is already infected, approach the healthy ones;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	And then dislocate it in the morning or the third day, and when you dislocate the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Change one bandage, and renew the salve (or dressing).
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts swell improperly after many days, know that the breasts do not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	If subtle poisons run after a long time, do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For the health approaches. There are men whose wounds heal slowly due to cold, and those who do the contrary;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the stomach swells excessively without reason after many days, know that the breasts are not affected;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breast delays in increasing, and it is swollen, let him apply dry and moist medicines that are moist in substance but dry in effect.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	As an eggshell defined, for it has a great part of vitreous [material], and it is the last remedy;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take eggshell defined, and make it with rose oil, and mix with old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook and use it; this same thing is better when boiled and thickened,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when eggshells defined are not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them together, and sprinkle the powder on honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then place one cloth, and lay it on the chest, and sometimes an Aristotle long-winded is administered;
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and root of celestial lily, which is like flour from many times and chalk.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and use of simple or compound remedies: grind them, make powder, and put on the honey that I said, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	And if the cure is prolonged, and not treated by this treatment.
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	Therefore, know that corruption begins in full, and presses on the bone or hard members, or ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment for the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess on the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Pancreatisis is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or under the toe, or perhaps it appears in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes inflamed, and no care is taken, one abscess may develop.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they will boil and discharge pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance it may break off completely.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And comes the corruption up to the bone, until it brings pain that smells bad, and the shoulders are wide apart, and the flesh is discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the previous section, but the treatment does not help at all.
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	Then you must cut away any excess that remains from the nail.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Next, cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is very great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail beneath the skin starts to push upwards and begins to swell, and blisters,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	you must place the rod under the nail so as not to pierce the skin.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	And strike it from above, and gently and lightly hit the flesh.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And place on top of the remaining flesh the medicine with burning and corrosive properties to remove all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it with onions until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	If the corruption is in the bone, strike and draw it out, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see the thigh to correct, strike it with a cupping glass as previously said,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wounded, bled, and causes great pain, then you must let it bleed first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then strike the nail with a sharp spatula from above in a crosswise manner,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	And keep the tip of the incision not to reach the flesh that is beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If it happens, place something on it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The patient who is born with tumors in his hands by accident is all fleshly.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	And by accident there may be a part where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	And none of these are born in the root of the joint, but rather they are born on some of our fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	The one born in any of the finger's knuckles does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	And he who is born at the joint of the thumb, by chance remains silent;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The weight of one who is fat is light, in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	weight him by his root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; cover it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or about to die, it is necessary that you cut round the flesh up to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and cure it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Fractures come together in the joints due to birth, injury, burns, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut the fracture so that it can heal in its natural shape;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two tents or dampened cloths oiled with rose oil, so that they do not stick together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	And you put thin wooden pieces between them until the joints are fastened as required.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If one of his hands comes with the palm towards the joint, you strike that joint as needed.
Des vils	Peasants
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large, swollen veins filled with melancholic excesses, which come in many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more often occurs in legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer purges of bile on occasion, and then heal with the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The iron cure is according to two methods: one is by hitting, and black blood is drawn out.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And another way is that you open the vein, and pull it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting is done in this manner: cut the leg open with hot sharp knife, until the flesh becomes thin.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then hold the patient's leg from above the knee down to the part below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then open the vein in one place, or two or three, of a large size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then slice and draw out the black blood from the vein to your hand, from one end to another, as much blood as the disease's strength can withstand.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it up, and instruct him to bind himself with black coloured meat for food.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and the healing when the veins are full, and it is beneficial for the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The swelling of it (the limb) is in this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair on it,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in water and raise the leg of hot water until it becomes red and swells the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you don't have water, then heat it with fire, and apply it to the vein along the thigh for a long time or in the part below the knee.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then scrape the skin with an awl and open the vein on both sides, until it appears when you feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And one sees it red and black, and when it enters or skin it seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then push the rod beneath [the dislocation], as long as it is raised from the skin, and then gently bend it to the point;
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then hit it in one other place about three fingers away; then cut open the skin over the vein as far as it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then sharpen the iron [instrument], as you have done, and bend it to another angle, as you did before.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then take another shape, or various [shapes] if needed, then sharpen, and bend it to the point of the shoulder,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then draw out and sharpen until the second shape; then cut it lengthwise, until it breaks completely, then bend it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	And if you cannot draw it out and lift it, push an awl with a thick, double thread into it.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And tie and pull it out, then push under a rod, and turn your hand back and forth until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And be careful that it does not break, for if it breaks, you cannot draw or lift it out, which causes harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have treated it completely, place over the wound a damp cloth soaked in vinegar and rose oil, and let it heal until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the face is contracted, twisted, and swollen together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	Then you must cut it painfully, but do not cover it; and pull it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to pierce the face is curved, but does not cut, that it should not pierce the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of large curve, because if it is delicate, it would pierce the vein; but be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is incised in the legs, in warm places where no grass or trees grow, and in land that has no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And in some cases it may arise elsewhere than the legs, which happens due to corruption that comes beneath the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	When a snake comes inside the body and goes forward, pierce between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a very large inflammation comes in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then the limb changes, and the vein begins to come out like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the shoulder is open, you should wrap around it a piece of wood from 1 to 1.5 cubits long and bind it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the wood on the leg, and every time it is pushed out of place, you should wrap it around the wood, and bind it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, you should cut a part of it, wrap the remaining part around it, but do not cover the root while it is still coming out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it returns into the flesh and causes abscesses, pus, or illness in that area.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Because of this thing it must be treated little by little until the head, and nothing remains on the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein when it is treated from five fingers' length, or ten,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and once a man came to me, whose it was ten fingers' length, and when you cut it, if you press one egg or pear, and pierce it to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	Empty everything within it; and let the material inside be voided, and bring in medicines that promote healing for three days, then heal as with an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes, many times to this vein, it opens at the joint of the foot or arm,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And it comes much of blood loss, and often bursts open; then heal it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called "cattle disease" in our land, because it often happens to cattle,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body spreading and multiplying,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it can be felt moving from member to member until it breaks through the skin or disappears.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And is an inflammation due to rottenness of some fluids, as worms, snakes, and tapeworms or belly ones come.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	Doubt is about its nature, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and comes to the oil,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	By chance, enters, and destroys the oil; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you wish to cure and drain it, one can do so only when he goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	then you must lie the limb above and below with a strong ligature tightly bound.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut across it and drain it forcefully, and if the wound is deep into the flesh, and you do not touch it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you cauterize it with fire until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm it does is that it runs oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near the oil, hold the scournel under it, then strike above and pull it out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and the patient should be cleansed of the body with soluble medicines to remove harmful humors.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And it bursts from the rotten flesh of meats.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "wakirir" on our land, and it is pain that comes in some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And then it moves from member to member; I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called upon a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	And after that, it began to rise like a worm at the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	As soon as nothing, just as sharp silver when it cuts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain spreads from that place and penetrates into the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And shortly after it runs through the entire body until it reaches the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then it was told to me that it would return again around the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how it moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Moreover, I had heard of pain moving from place to place.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it in a woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	And I thought it was because the woman had a dry body, and the veins exposed.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason that condition appears constricted.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear accordingly to those who are delicate, and have moist bodies and veins covered.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see treating this disease, and the patient feels that pain as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	If the joint above and below is pressed hard, then press on it until the windiness (swelling or inflammation) is forced back to its place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the affected area; if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	use the remedy for those who swell up, such as pills made from pennyroyal or snakeweed, and similar remedies.
Des saiettes	Arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their shapes and according to the places in the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity among them is that some have large points, and small, and blunt, and solid ones.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those with two points, and of those with tongues, and of those where there are fragments.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and when an arrow strikes any member, it does so in two ways: either in the principal part (where it pierces),
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Like a brain, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls out of place in any of these organs, and the signs of death that I will tell you afterwards will indicate:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you must perform the extraction of this arrow, because death comes in many ways afterward.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not completely out, pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And when the head of the skull is pierced by an arrow and passes through it, a blow that is above the skull should be applied.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	When there is a cataract and scalding and hemorrhaging and inflammation of the tongue, and convulsions and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps without force from the nostrils, or ears; and perhaps loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	Jumps out of the wound white moisture like pus, and also jumps like burned charcoal.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	If this sign appears to you, refrain from treatment, and draw the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it falls or pierces, is that it is near the left breast, and feels like it has been driven into something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance, the patient becomes mute like the hair, and in a black cold blood comes sweating, and coldness and faintness follow.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then it is clear that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of the arrow that has pierced the flesh is without bubbles jumping from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and breathes heavily and seeks for the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the bed of hay, it is buried in the ribs; and it emits a great groan and great pain and breaths heavily; and all the members of the shoulder move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or food remains stuck in the wound, by chance anything from undigested meat may jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach, and something from the undigested intestines jumps out of the wound, there is no hope for the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow strikes the bladder and urine jumps out and escapes, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members such as the face and neck, shoulder and back, chest and arms, spine of the back, pelvis and legs, and similar limbs are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, for this reason you should do something else.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man that an arrow fell or pierced the root of his nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I pulled it out from the other side under the fat of the ear and it came out painlessly.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And drew another arrow that fell in the fat of the oil under the paper below,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow was reinserted, and it could not be drawn out except by the tip towards the flesh,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was big like a Turkish bow, with all one iron head slightly curved towards the ears; the patient was healthy, and no bad accident happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And it passed through an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow had ears (feathers) on it:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was bearded, and sharpened it so much that I passed it through, and the Christian remained healthy.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And take out an arrow from a person who was shot or stabbed, thinking he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after thirty days, his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut across the arrow, removed it carefully, and there was no adverse consequence.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if a person has an arrow lodged in his back, and the wound is sutured;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	And the arrow remained inside [the body], and did not change its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor did it cause any harm in any of its natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And saw another man who was wounded by an arrow in his body, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained thus with great pain for a long time; and many other similar things happened.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And draw an arrow from a knight of the king who was struck within the neck,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrowhead was fully embedded
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to attend to the wound after it had been three days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I pierced it with a thin needle and felt no pain at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	He feels prickling and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was the tip of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I placed a plaster compressing and digestive medicine on the injured area since it did not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	The tip of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I place the plaster on the wound daily, and straighten the injury right away, and keep it in that condition for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until it feels the arrow within its neck for an entire day; and he tells me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I place the medicine on the wound that is corrosive by hand until it is open
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried, and felt the head of the arrow that was fitting to the place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then align in the opening of the wound with that astringent medicine, until the head of the arrow becomes visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and passed beyond the limits for four months.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	Then I cut open the wound where I had inserted the pincers, from one side and the other, but it could not be closed.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I did not cease to refine and devise means with various instruments until I took [the arrow] with well-made pincers for one day.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to its shape that will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I hold it, and return the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I shall restore it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was entirely well.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	I have told you about the extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	if you apply your treatment to this (thing) which I am not saying, for books cannot fully grasp it.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters can compare themselves on very little things and on what is present and failing.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	three works (or nine) are necessary, and nine tools, for the reduction of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not come out of limbs where they are inserted except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	Through which part they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which is thrust through there where it enters, it is an arrow entering into the flesh, and at times it may pierce suddenly.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not pierce suddenly, let it remain until the flesh is swollen around it and the opening is closed;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And similarly, if it [the dislocation] is driven into the bone and cannot come out, leave it for some days and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	Then it jumps and if it does not jump, perforate around with a sharp needle everywhere the joint is enlarged, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is driven into the skull bone and goes to one of the brain's ventricles,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	And some of the accidents that I have said open to the patient: do not draw it out at all, but let it remain even for some days.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if the arrow comes so close, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	If the arrow is not driven into the flesh but only in the bone and does not come close to the surface,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And the patient remains for some days without a bad incident, if they manage to endure the extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be extracted, administer a plaster around it, as I told you earlier; then heal the wound when it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged inside the body and cannot be seen, search for it with all your strength;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel (it), pull it with any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	If the pain prevents you from pulling (it) due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if there is no bone, nerve or vein, open (the wound) as much as the pain allows.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	And pull out the arrow if possible, and if there are ears on the arrow (to hold it in place),
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	If the bone which is pierced by two parts through the muscle that you can feel,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the arrowhead, as much as you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow, but pull it out more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, press the arrowhead against the bones around it, then pull it out, as extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood obstructs [the process], bring forth what we have said in the chapter regarding its treatment;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of incising the nerve and the vein, and put device as you can pull out the arrow safely,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; place the patient according to the shape he was in when the arrow hit him,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	because it is the greatest help that can be, and if you cannot do so, leave him according to what the signs indicate to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, opens any part of it, or the leather is swollen in one place as we can see or feel apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Then cut across [the arrow], until the tongs can grasp it, and then pull it out; if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round as much as it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then continue the extraction until it issues forth.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	If it is of the arrow shaft, push it all the way through.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if it is fallen, and you see a remedy for it, administer it. If there is one, apply a hair-based remedy.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters the hair of the remedy; and then push it through.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if the arrowhead is pointed, push an instrument with a sharp point entering, to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrowhead is touched, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as required.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow pierces or penetrates the abdomen or bladder or side, and it is close, and you can cover over it, then cover it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And be careful not to cut the vein and the nerve, then pull it out, and then make an incision, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Cure it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to extract arrows are similar to an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the buttock hair is similar to the feather of a bird.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	To point the arrowhead, as it should be shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the forceps (tongue-like instrument) for insertion and removal is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	openings of the body's common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	openings from which one bleeds are 31, of which there is a main artery 16.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This means: there are two bands that are after the ears, which are called "the double 'herbech'"
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	And the two arteries which are in the two temples appear;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And the two veins that are in the two eyelids, called "aspirates";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the neck of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two tendons that are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	And the two veins which are above the lips, on the mouth, are called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And the two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins, which are commonly bled, are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	The first is the cephalic, which lies on the left side, and common people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle part is called "fast," and is composed of the cephalic and the basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And the common people call it "vein of the belly," and it is above the liver.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And it is that one bleeds from, which opens clearly above the groin.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the little vein is the one that is between the auriculare and anularis, and it has two rain(s).
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and foot are four veins: one is beneath the shinbone of the left thigh,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second shinbone that is at the wrist of the right arm; and the vein called "ness", which is in the wrist of the other arm.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg are four veins underneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The evacuation of veins located behind the ears helps with old-style purgatives and emigration.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the bloodletting, as I tell you, are that you raise the patient's head.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Whenever you feel a lump under your skin, and where you sense the pulse beneath your skin, press it firmly.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet and push it through under the vein up to the bone, then pull your hand all along the vein.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and the skin and the vein about two fingers deep, and make the blood come out as you see fit.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then bind it and let it heal.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The ligation of the two arteries that are in the temples is equivalent to migraine treatment in ancient times.
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and softening, and common ophthalmia, and in the chest of the eyes with watery discharge.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	The qualities of ligature are as follows:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And it is that the patient stretches his neck, until the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulsation beneath your throat, and then press down on it;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the cure (or dressing) over the vein to the top of your throat indicator, and push the lancet under it;
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	lift the vein up, and tie it off, as you have done with the other veins, and make a knot in the blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, and put your hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on top of it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Then form the wound and let it heal; and we have spoken about its covering and its extraction, where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the healing of the head in the ancient diseases of the face and migration and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And the quality is that the patient tilts his neck, twisting it until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called "fosseur", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and allow blood to flow according to the amount you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein when it is healthy and never use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Furthermore, the flames should not be too sharp, and it is better to proceed obliquely because the bone is close, and there is danger of breaking the flame when it is narrow.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The salve of the two veins which are in the two armholes helps with swelling, inflammation, redness, and the diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of its salve are that the patient stretches their neck by twisting it with some rope, as previously mentioned;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then place the salve, and let the salve be made from across [the neck], a piece of flax about a foot long and wide, for there is no heat in it.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps they break; then make a tourniquet of blood, as much as you need, and then tie it up with linen, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The venous vein of the neck is beneficial for agues, scrofula, and febrile diseases.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	as in migraines and redness that comes with fever, especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the vein is such that the patient compresses his neck, then compresses his neck with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	And take the subtle flame long, and thrust it into the space between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	For if the vein does not open well in that, and the wound begins to fester now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	do not go too far in, and make the bleeding according to your necessity, then let it rest for a night, for it is soon restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The first joints of the two knees aid in the straightening of the shinbone, and at the beginning of swelling, and in many diseases, and in impetigo, and in corrosion, and in herpes, and in inflammations.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of the joint are such that the patient draws his neck under one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master stand on top of the patient's head, and the patient sit on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then open the vein along its length with a small gap, then drain the blood gently, as needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then repair the damage on the other vein, then cut the ligament, and press and tighten the veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	do not let the patient strangle (the wound); and leave it until morning, so that the wound heals.
De la sainie des leivres	On Curing Swords (wounds)
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The saliva from the veins of the lips above helps to clot in the mouth and contributes to the corruption of gums, fissures in lips, and tooth and surrounding issues.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the saliva are to make the patient sit before you and hold his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	And they (the dislocations) are recognized by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that there are small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	examine them carefully and if you do not recognize them or have doubts,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	press the larger one (of the two), and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From under the tongue:
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The first aid for veins located under the tongue assists after the cephalic (head) wound, and it is in the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the siphon are that the patient must sit between your hands in front of the sun, and lift the tongue, and look under each side to find a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	therefore, one and the other, but do not go too deep, because beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins from which we commonly heal are healed according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or in pricking with all one large flame, or olive oil subtle as you know to cauterize, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirrhine is very famous, and it is wide as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it must be used to open the veins with large amounts of obvious blood, which contain much blood and turbulence.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And this is the form of the olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is pointed more precisely, and is for thinning the subtle veins where there is fine yellow blood.
