Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The sanctuary vein, which is one of those veins, helps with the diseases that are located under the throat, neck, and abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the lord to bleed profusely, and to let blood from the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if it touches the artery, bleeding occurs, which must be stopped as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And it should not be pricked with fire, but cut as with a surgical instrument.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open clearly, then you must open it, and change another one. (In context of medical treatment, likely referring to opening a bone to treat an injury)
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or if you wish any relief from it, or if you are sick in the place of it, the vein opens clearly in the arm. (In context of treating an injury, likely referring to finding a vein)
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the fire cautery as we have said before. (In the context of medical treatment, possibly referring to using heat therapy for various ailments)
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to find the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you dislocate the arm and touch the place until you recognize the pulse. (In context of medical treatment, likely referring to locating a vein for bloodletting)
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then sign the joint with ink, then tie the arm, and burn the vein with a hot iron.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And be careful not to cut into the artery when you see the joint swollen, for it is an artery; then avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	If you see it rising high like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is not from an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Then take your finger and hold it long over the place, then cut your finger until it stops bleeding, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Let the arm remain still, and do not move it; let the patient not move it until he is healthy and free from fear.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the wound is not cauterized and it starts to bleed, and there is no medicine present, then seize the artery if it opens up, as it can be stopped by compressing it; stop the bleeding of the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of fig bark and cut it in half, and take one of the halves and place it on top until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it (the wound) does not stop bleeding, that's good; if it does not, treat it as we have said with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stopping of bleeding is not always effective in many positions due to the small size of the wound and the slender nature of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The bleeding from a vein in the middle helps to treat blood in the head above and in the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and the cephalic, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And it is necessary for the lord [physician] to bore through [make an incision] along the nerve that lies beneath, and if he pierces too deep, and finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the patient becomes sickly, and possibly cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens frequently, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, you must use the instrument cautery to burn it; strip away the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make an incision along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The bleeding of the head, if it draws blood from the head, helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to cauterize with olive oil or myrtle fire, because it is the safest of all veins, since there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Furthermore, it is necessary to seek the easier joint, and not harm anything if it must be done for the first time, and one repeats.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Moreover, sometimes the joints swell in some men, when it must be done for the first time, but one should not harm anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound, according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about healing wounds is that healing them is not done except for the sake of health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid future diseases.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the healing be made in one of the four veins that are called: cephalic, femoral, or basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And one should bleed at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And one should bleed every third or fourth day, two hours after or three days afterwards.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding given for diseases is not assigned an hour limit, but when it is needed, either during the day or at night, in all hours and every moment.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And one should not bleed children under the age of twelve or pregnant women during the first four months up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	The patient who have passed sixty years, should not heal themselves.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when some wish to heal themselves in any way, it is necessary that their intestines be cleansed with a light enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if there are many worms retained within, so that the veins do not carry away the waste products from the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	The patient who are too salted in meats, or drunk, to such an extent that they vomit, or have dropsy:
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if there is a surgeon after colic suffering, vomiting, abdominal disorder, excessive intercourse with women, labor, watching, and praying, or any weakness caused by the weapon or the body,
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then purify the humors, if it is fat, with food and drinks and medicines, if you have that power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then in a bath, without anything preventing, to purify the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	And heal the vein with the pit (cautery) as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And keep him that day from labor, and from pricking, and from lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	Be bound and cheerful, and let the healer be higher than him who is being healed, and rub the arm twice or thrice.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then remove the ligature gently, for if it is too tight or loose, it cannot heal correctly.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the place with hands until the veins swell, and feel it.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then moisten the warmers with a little old oil, then place your thumb of your left hand over that vein under the place where you want to heat,
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	that the vein does not burst and break when cutting it.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins which run like cords in a sieve, and some of these are filled with windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	if when heat is applied, it draws back from the fire, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is one of these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	if it opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, for which reason the surgeons should be advised in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it's good; but if not, start again a little below or above that place where it is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen and the patient fears, let it rest for one or two days and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	In case pusules come up, do not enter or take a bath, then start the healing process if it pleases the patient.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	If the wound is small or if you doubt that it will not bleed much as you see, pour hot water directly into the wound itself.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And it is worked a little hastily, so that the joint is inflamed; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the joint inflamed, do not begin healing immediately, but put a little oil on it, for the blood is cooled and the oil heals in this place.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And administer the oil in this manner in every bleeding that you heal the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And this same thing causes a triple fracture and a dislocation of the joint, when it is put back in its place; if it is too subtle, it separates again when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, especially when the opening of the vein is small.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you hurry, put a wet sponge in hot oil and hold it for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it is necessary that you do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in its place after some days without any blackness or greenness, it does not matter.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, place something of aloes or myrrh below the wound, on a poultice or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess and appearance occur in the church's sanctuary: place your hand on it then, and if you find it soft under the pressure of your hand, this is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then do not place anything above what has been said, for in court without the artery; but make one dry plaster to harden it, then treat with other treatment until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each according to the amount of its power and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it becomes red; and if you see it large, let it become thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for those who are filled and hollowed out, and have need of bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and let the veins be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for those who are weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to let them bleed little by little, and it should be done by making small incisions across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bloodletting is safe from displacement of blood and damage to nerves, and it is more beneficial than long bloodletting or wide bloodletting.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one whose body requires healing, it is necessary to give soft bread below grape-like fruits; if it is boiled, bleed three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If it is of cold complexion, eat soft bread in syrup sweetened with honey or aromatic syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, cloves and a pleasant smelling syrup before the healing process.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	If it is bleeding from a wound during the healing process, after the flow of blood, it is necessary that he drinks broth of meat and subtle-smelling syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And use other things as we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If one wants to burst open his arm or bleed elsewhere when weakened by repeated bleeding, it should be done little by little, according to the amount of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	If one wishes to burst open his arm after the first bleeding and has a strong heart, he should wait 6 hours following the first bleeding or the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	If one wishes to bleed elsewhere, it should be done on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood within the body that is already heated and causes fever; therefore, it is necessary to draw a large quantity of it and widen the opening until it can pass through easily.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you reward all the conditions of health, and place your hand over the thumb when it heals, so that death does not come in its place.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times when healers are negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not appropriate when you see to dislocate the arm, and make blood come out a second time, and the wound has closed, that you press firmly.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	And if it is curved, that you extend the arm forcefully, for it would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave it until the blood comes out a second time; or you prick at the tip of the flame, so that the frozen blood from the vein flows away.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on it one piece of fresh linen dipped in vinegar and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is open, do not restrain it but let it be until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to draw blood a second time, do it in the same place where it was drawn before, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is connected to the vein of the head because they are composed of the same material.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the way to draw blood is that the patient pushes their hand into hot water until the flesh becomes red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then it shall be tied moderately, so that the vein appears clearly, then press gently through across, neither too wide nor too long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the wounds be opened widely, and press firmly near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be drawn out, place the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow out into the hot water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is hot, do not strike the hand with hot water, for one places more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the vein of this [specific] vessel is safer than all other vessels, as there are no artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the cephalic vein on the right hand is useful for all liver diseases, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand and push into sharp hot, until the vein is emptied, if you see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the wound is transverse, and if you close it completely, it causes no harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And do not go too deep, for nerves are all beneath the skin exposed.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Then place the hand in hot water, so that it does not freeze in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let the blood as needed, put oil and linen on the wound to heal quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The purgation of the left hand's skin is beneficial for the disease of the mice, and do as I told you regarding the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The purge of the sofflene is useful for all the diseases that are under the body.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as the diseases of the belly, and retention of flowers, and diseases of the genitals, and the thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the qualities of its purge are that the patient puts his foot in hot water and scratches on the vein until it bursts,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And lay it above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there are many streams flowing.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Close it then with a larger vein, or at the ankle, since that is more effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	If you close it above the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath, and close it through as in cutting; and let the flames be still.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If the wound does not heal, immerse the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if lancing is required for the first time, begin the second one a little above, since the area is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not be afraid of nerves, as we have said, and proceed similarly with the tendon of the other side equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The area of the sciatic vein is at the ankle joint, and lancing it relieves the pain of the heel when it is hot with blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	The quality of its lancing is that the patient immerses themselves in water and pulls upwards on the ankle four fingers' width while twisting it.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, heal it in all ways that you can, and crosswise.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	It is more suitable that you cauterize it, for the wound is exposed, and it is very difficult to treat by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not cauterize it, there will be no healing of the wound that opens or its edge, and towards the little finger, and guard against nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And make as much correction to the blood as you see, then undo the ligature and put on cotton and bind it; the wound is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	From the blisters (of ventouse)
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Blisters (of ventouse) are made of horns, or hog's bristles, or glass; and ventosation is done according to two methods: either by wounding and drawing blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventosation which is done without wounding has two methods: either it is heated over all fire, or with fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and ventosation which is done by wounding and drawing blood is made in twelve parts of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	The first one is all in a sleep, the other one is on the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And the two others on both sides of the neck; and the abscesses under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the abscesses in the armpits, and the abscesses on the knees;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And boils appear on both arms; and boils on both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the blisters of the wrists; and blistering does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered on the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason you should not lance them at all, as done with venesection of veins;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered in any disease that comes from repletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if necessary due to illness it is required to bleed, or as custom dictates, we will administer it every hour at the beginning or end of the month, and in between and at any time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need to bleed, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if there are those who find swelling and reddening in their face, head, neck, and darkness of the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have bitten their tongue, and swallow blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if there are such people who think and see signs such as numbness, loss of sensation, fainting, and death-like symptoms.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially during the month, we order to have them bled after 4 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bloodletting from the menses helps with headaches that come from the eyes, and it is not necessary to do so after the evacuation of the entire body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	And this ventosation is in the position of the head of the cervical.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it must not be used by someone with a cold constitution or who has catarrh, because it causes them much harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore, the elderly should not use it, nor those with a cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And if one heals often from it, they become numb, and therefore, the ventosation must be placed a little lower due to the fear of numbness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The ventosation (a procedure or condition) is located at the neck and base of the skull, and for this reason it is suitable for traction of the neck.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to cut the canal of the vertebrae, and immediately, and to fill (it).
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should be pushed gently, for if it holds too firmly, it may cause obstruction of the intestines or stomach.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventosations at the two ribs of the neck are good for headaches, migraines, strangulations, and pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is in the position of the basilica's sanctuary; you must command the lord to extend his hand to place it, not to strike the artery, and there should be no bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Wind-tunnels under the chin are useful for mouth diseases, tooth decay, and similar mouth illnesses; they are in the position of the sinuses of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Wind-tunnels in the shoulders are useful for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventosations of the sides are worth as much as three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the Lord not to draw too deeply because the limb is naked of flesh, and it knows nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventosation on the buttocks is worth as much as the emorroid operations at their foundation, and for diseases below, and it must be large and made of horsehair, which needs to be drawn well, and if it were too thin, it would break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The swellings of the legs open widely because they attract blood from all over the body, and they are similar to ancient pains in the sides, hips, and bladder, and they reduce the flow of fluids; they are located at the junctions of the shins and ankles, and they weaken the body after a long time, and bring pus into various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to treat the swelling is that you first evacuate it and immediately apply a warm substance, press it quickly, move it evenly, and do not stop doing so until you see the redness and swelling subside, and the redness of the blood appears; then bandage it, and take care in the position of the body, because there are some who have hard flesh and clear pores: it is necessary to wound only once, and it is necessary to make wide incisions, but not too deep; and evacuate gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is large, it is necessary to make two incisions: the first one to refine the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the bone is very thick, it must be struck three times; and when we want to draw blood drop by drop, we should prick only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	If we want a lot of blood, we should repeat frequently; and if the bone is thick, we strike to the end, and it should be done so that the veins are pricked suddenly,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for those with thick and hard skin, and with narrow pores, to anoint the joints of the fingers with sharp and dissolving oil.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is to be anointed, use violet oil, almond oil, or oil made from the seeds of a squash.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is to be applied with grease, use watercress oil, lily oil, chamomile oil, or any similar oil.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amaranth oil or balsam oil, anise oil, and any similar oil.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person to be healed has thin skin and large pores, no oil should be applied.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But it is necessary to wash after the dislocation with rose water, or cold water, or water of morello cherries, or water of gourds, or water of porcelain, or any similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from ashes or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large excesses should rise from old wine, or vinegar water, or a decoction of fennel or chamomile, or similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	And it is not advisable to bleed with a cupping glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and do not sleep after cupping.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it is necessary that he urinate, when he should be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	Watch out for the one who bleeds is bilious, and he without is too sharp and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	He should take cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, and lettuces to cool, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And piglets, and beef from a cask, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold constitution, may take syrup made from honey and aromatic wine diluted between old and new, and eat porridge, and piglets, and small birds and young birds.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day he purges himself, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	it is necessary to give some men three times triacet or muscat before purging, or after, to strengthen the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And let the drink be made subtle, but it should not be drunk by those who are hot.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The blisters that are placed to wound are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and podagra, and on the abdomen and the flank and the legs and the hips, because these limbs cannot bear to be wounded there.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it should not be done to draw blood from one member to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we do with the testicles when they are swollen; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just as we place blisters on the abdomen and the flank to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And remove the pain when there is an obstruction or arrow, it removes by chance the obstruction or displaces the arrow from its place with its virtue.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And thus it acts when put on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these winds are administered empty to suck only; sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	As in diseases of the eyes, and in such a way that the wind tube is filled with hot water or water in which herbs such as comfrey have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the blister to be treated with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	It should be two fingers wide and half a palm in depth, and it should have one small hole around the middle, just like pushing an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and be made of linen, soft in front so as not to burn the patient when placed on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and in the middle have a rod of iron or linen, to put a plaster bandage around it.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And they are great and small according to the diseases and age of those who suffer from them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the boils of children are different than those of the old, and those of the thin than those of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And this boil should be placed upon the member in such a way:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Apply the wax candle or linen thread, and place it through the cork of the syringe that is inside the syringe.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is within the cork of the syringe so as not to burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the member, and your fingers should be above the wound as we have said, so that when one looks at it, if the vapor is there, remove the syringe.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the linen thread again as before, repeating it as often as needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the blister given in the disease of pleurisy, there is neither rod nor puncture, and it is not applied except when it is full of water, and is placed on the member only.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Blisters are not applied except in members where it is not possible to place a blister due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the bare skin of the eye, such as eyelid or nose, and other similar places.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the qualities of the patient are such that when you find wounds clean, in sweet clear waters without putrefaction, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and immerse them in a clean fresh water until they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	Then it should be purged with vein and blisters, then rub the member until it turns red, and place the wounds on top.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they become swollen and hot, if it is possible to apply a bladder (ventouse), do so, as it works well.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the limb above ground level and then immerse in warm water, then apply a poultice.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	If the limbs remain too long without blood flow, immerse one linen cloth in cold water and place it on top until the blood returns.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if there are no bones (sans) multiplied (multipliez), place it on broken glass or plaster, and similar things, until it is heated (estenchiez).
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or you place half of boiled beans on the affected area and leave them until they harden (s'aerdent) to the affected area, it will stop now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more, take other beans.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the beans do not want to be taken, rub the affected area with fresh blood, or you pierce it with a needle until the bones come out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And then place them on top (of each other), and as soon as they feel the blood, they will harden;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are bleeding, sprinkle some powder of aloe and of linen (or ash), or charcoal on them, then they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the treatment of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Inform the dear boy that foolish men fall from this chapter, who have never seen any old books or read a single letter of them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, the science is estranged in our land, for I have never found anyone good at it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it, except by the science of the old books, where I have studied the science so much that I have treated it, and by experience, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described for you in this chapter what is contained within it, and have summarized it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are brought, just as I have done in these two chapters beforehand.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we say the prologue of this book the number of words and the chapters where wise men put their understanding, and dwell on truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	When fracture, dislocation, twisting or curvature comes to anyone, it is necessary that you straighten the patient from one side and the other, unless something prevents you, such as weakness of body, infants, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the time is not very urgent or too cold; and avoid cold joints, that is to say cold fingers and wrists, and do not drink wine, nor consume any greasy meat, and do not fill oneself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about hot abscess or spreading of matter in the member; if the patient returns to its former state of health as it has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that cause thick mucus, such as cooked wheat in water and broth, meat, heads, feet, beef, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For thick nourishment strengthens and heals the broken bones more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	Know that the broken bones of old and weak people cannot be easily healed or mended according to their nature due to the looseness of the members, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	However, it has no cure, reset on the broken bone, that is large splints which tighten and join the limb together, until it heals as before; and do not apply any other treatment, and for this reason feed him with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is other than the break of the foot, or leg; and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to the joint, and another growing sharper, like the tip of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a break with a wound, then it is a break with a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in every way has its tool and instrument for restoration, according to what memory comes to mind.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known as the fracture of the bone by this: the joint is twisted and opens widely through breaking, and sounds on pressure from the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And if there is no twisting nor touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it may have twisting, splitting, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move the hand yourself, but put on the medicines that come after this, and then gently tighten it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fractures that go to the joints, and are the two parts disjoined, it is necessary now to set them equally, in this way abscesses will grow well.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses come, let it be left for some day, until the abscess is soothed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then set it equally in the position that you can easily and wisely move, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration of one where there are fragments; then tighten it as needed hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into pieces and it breaks in two, whether it's a hand or foot, or to your hand when it is a small member, or two cords, or one cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you reset with all tools possible the additions in their places as much as you can, and be careful not to cause injury or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	align well the two shoulder bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand if it seems not well to you: straighten it properly, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who bring it by their work abscess heat and contraction to the member, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	When the limb is set, correctly keep the patient from moving it, neither watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And ensure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it is not in the correct position, it must be put into such a position that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and ensure that it is set right, that twisting does not come when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken limb are as I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs can be of various kinds, large or small, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and fingers etc.; it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those which are thick, such as the thigh and leg: it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and hard linen, for the large linens embrace the whole large member and tighten all parts equally, so that there is no pain.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then wrap light poultices around it, 3 or 4 times according to the member, and tighten your hand a little on the entire linen, then go above the break and tighten less than the break, then move away from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the ligament bit by bit and bit by bit, until you take a large part of the healthy flesh, then take another ligament and turn it right around the broken bone.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go to the part below the break, and tighten it moderately, neither too strong nor too loose, as we have said in the first lesson above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place dampened linen or cloth strips between the ligaments until they are all even, then bind everything with a bandage on top, and then put well-made splints on if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, place hot soothing things on it to ease the abscess, and wait several days for it to heal.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then hold your arms straight, with the elbows forming half the length of a thick cane, or from a club used for splitting logs, or with palm-sized branches, and in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but the arm that you put on the fracture should be slightly larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and it should be as long as is required for a member, whether large or small.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then hold above the shoulders, just like you did at the first stage, then tie on a thread coming from above, as in the first stage on the fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	Then bind it closer, but not too tight; and it should be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of flax.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their bindings with twisted flax ropes, and this is a great error, because the binding cannot be even if it is too thin, and it should not have less than two fingers' space between each shoulder.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the heads of arrows after resetting the shoulder in a healthy state, place linen or linen bandages under them so they do not fester.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the veins are broken, I will tell the cure afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	Know this: it is not necessary to bind all broken limbs tightly on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to put hot irons on them before 5 or 7 days, or more according to your certainty of the abscess healing.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and here is the manner of old plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: and it is that you take flour that is kept near the mill walls, and mix it with a lot of egg, and put this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring the fracture in many ways, and equally for women and small children, as it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plaster for restoring fractures and dislocations and twists: take aloes, linseed oil, turpentine, balm of Gilead, mastic, in equal amounts; myrrh and aloeswood, 5 times the amount; and seven times as much alum; make powder from them, mix with enough egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, as it has a good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and it benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster that is effective for twisting: take mugwort and mastic, mix together 10 parts; add mirrh and aloes, mix together 8 parts; add acacia wood, 6 parts; Armenian bole, 10 parts, grind well and infuse with vinegar or abundant egg white, administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method for joints and dislocated bones: take new linen, soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, apply it on the affected area. This plaster does not restore [the damage], but it is good for easing hot abscess pain, and proper treatment for bone pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster for broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earthy parsley, grind them together to make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of bone fracture and for improving abscess healing. Take root of comfrey, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of beans, of each one part; grind them and mix with wine, and if the members are scalded, mix it with moist coriander water or vinegar and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another stronger method of plaster for the restoration of the limb when a hard abscess comes up. Take roots of comfrey, flax seed, balm of Gilead, lentil, and wormwood, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all one part; grind them and mix with salty water, sweet water, or vinegar, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that nothing but a beeswax and oil ointment should be put on the broken member for restoration, and no other thing more, and says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that one should place warm, slightly dry things on the broken limb to restore it, such as myrrh, aloes, incense and similar substances, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat a wound and pain: take ground mugwort and horse hooves that have been boiled, or feathers of birds, and sow thistle, equal amounts, grind them and make a poultice out of it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then wait a little while, and make sure the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place. If not, do not dislocate it by hand for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain or itching comes to the joint, or there is no rest or swelling, then hurry and dislocate it, and remove the plaster immediately; and take a light cloth, and a damp sea sponge, and dip in water, and raise the joint until the itching stops, and the pain is eased.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry linen on it, dampened in water or rose oil, and tie it up tightly until you are sure of stopping the abscess from heating.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Let the inflammation of the limb rest, and let the pain cease, then begin to tie it up gently, and a little plaster, and do not strain it too much as before; and tie it up finely until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess swells and reddens and hurts, and it needs to be lanced and sutured, proceed as you did the first time equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing comes to the limb of what we have said, do not undress it before 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days; and sometimes leave it for 20 days as one sees fit, until the swelling subsides and the abscess approaches the skin.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then keep it more tightly bound than the first time, and let the meat swell, as I have said before; and if you see the wound dry out more than necessary, know that pus cannot come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Arise then from hot moist heat, every time you dislocate it, and for each third day, wet a little the joint.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	By this work then cut the nerves in the limb, and correct immediately those that are crooked by the foolish doctor, who leave it twisted: this is harmful, and it is a dangerous procedure; I see nothing but laziness and working incorrectly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many kinds of fractures are, and they have various shapes, and their causes are intended.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	because there are fractures made by sword impact, and the collar bone breaks the entire bone up to the shaft which is under the bone, as happens with a hacksaw or fist; this type of fracture is called "hack-fracture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	when the sword strikes the bone from above it pierces through, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and these two types of fractures are either large or small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion filled, or cut, or from wounds of stone, or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if the break penetrates through to the membrane under the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is sunk into the bone as fine as a hair and the cut is small, and because of this it is called this break "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by hitting with stone, or falling, or similar things, and drives the bone piece inward, and the pieces of the bone are closely packed together like a potter when he puts them into pots; if the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in those who have a moist skull bone, such as an infant's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	Also, it happens with all these types of breaks that small fragments are dislocated, as is the case here. I shall speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all types of breaks through dissection above them, and the examination by probing, and the corruption of the flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is known to those who, when the bone has been exposed and rubbed inward, if it opens the black crack will appear.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be careful about the patient's condition, and if you see any harmful symptoms like vomiting of blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, fainting, high fever, hairs falling out and turning red, and other similar signs in various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any doubtful symptoms and hope for salvation, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound first comes to you in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth moon within which you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone is corrupted, and come the events we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone fracture reaches the tissue that covers the brain, you must cut the broken part in such a way: it is that you take hold of the patient's head firmly, and peel off the skin over the bone in every possible way, and above the wound more gently than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if the discharge of blood comes to uncover the bone or an abscess forms, use whatever is necessary and fill the area with damp linen soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And let the wound rest until the abscess subsides and you are assured of the stopping of blood flow; then begin around the bone to remove, and it is done according to two ways of work: one way is that you cut narrowly in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have various incisions, some narrow and others wide, pointed and made with iron instruments; and work lightly, so that you do not wound the bone.
