Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is protruding and hard, you must pierce around it, so that you administer incisions with drills, not cutting through the bone of the head, but having a margin or circle above the point to prevent the drill from passing through the bone; and you must have several, so that each one comes in its place along the length of the bone, so that you have drills for all sides; and this is the shape of the four types of drills.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for drilling around the broken bone are that you place one drill on the bone and turn it with your hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then move the drill to another part a little afterwards, and do this all around, then remove the chips of the bone that are between the holes, and do this as delicately and lightly as possible, as we have said, until you pull out the bone or any of the instruments you have such as pliers or forceps; and be careful not to touch the brain or the marrow.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have drilled the bone and treated it, it is necessary that you remove the splinter left in the bone with another instrument resembling an incisor, but it should be thinner and more delicate than the other incisors.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if there remains something of small bones or no scales, lightly cut them with an instrument; then heal the wound with dressings and salves as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of work is that which the Greeks call (it), which is more reliable; and it is highly praised, and this is its statement.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, you must expose part of the bone where the fracture is visible, so that when you have exposed that part, place it under the tip of the chisel-like instrument as shown in this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut it from one side, and the part is in two edges, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then hit with a small hammer on top, so that you lightly cut the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is gouged into the bone, then cut it gently, because one cuts bones unnecessarily and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the fracture does not pierce through to the cloth and the bone is only chopped from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to smooth that roughness, and remove scales with a sharp scraper of various sizes, in order to provide the most suitable amount, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	The patient should shave his head completely first with a large razor, then with finer ones afterwards, and continue to do so until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each other kind of haircut and subtle break, you must bring the instrument according to his discretion; and this is not a matter that can be answered by one who has not studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is open, you must take one linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, wet it in rose oil and place it on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another cloth doubled in 1 or 3 layers, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this as lightly as possible, so as not to weigh it down, then administer another thread over it, but don't pull it tight more than needed just to cover the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And leave it for 1 or 2 days, until the abscesses have subsided, then remove the thread, and administer medicines such as lily roots, flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder from these things, and place it on the wound, and administer immediate medicines without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And watch that the wound remains clean, do not leave any ointment or allow pus to collect, for when pus collects on the fabric of the cloth, it corrupts and rots, causing great harm to the patient; for when something biting is placed over the wound, it causes further harm.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, this is cause for doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if it comes from anything other than the medicine we have placed on it, which has this virtue, you must take a part of honey, and 3 parts of rose oil and in a linen cloth dipped in it, and apply it to the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound as necessary, until it heals.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose are broken, or one part alone, because there are two bones; and the one beneath is cartilage, which does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should insert your little finger or thumb into the nostril, and place the break equidistant from your index finger and the corner of the mouth, pushing it out as the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and watch that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and the finger cannot reach it, you should place a small stick equal to the height of the root of the finger there.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is of two parts, do so again, and hurry to restore it in the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has settled down, then apply the linen bandage to the head of the neck where the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you place another on the other side if there is a break there; and let the bandages be as thick as they fill the neck openings.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they said that any restorer should moist the bandages with butter and change them every day. I do not think it is good, but it is necessary for them to be moistened in an ointment made of egg yolk and flour, and then leave the bandage until the bone has hardened and the cartilages have become hard.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes feathers from an owl are put in place of tents, and if it is covered with a thin cloth, and the opening is held closed, breath the patient through; then do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes out while you are working on it, put beeswax or cotton wool soaked in rose oil, or a pinch of sulphur there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	If the abscess does not come out, put a plaster on the outside, made of wheat flour and incense powder, mixed with egg white, then place light stops on top but do not tie it down.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the break in the neck is small, and it is broken into many pieces, extract them with suitable instruments, then make the incision, and cure the injuries with charms, salves, and ointments suitable for the case.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound within the neck, cure it with linen and apply plasters until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	on the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated beneath [something], and there is no wound outside, and the break is only outside, but not broken through, unless hollow inside, it can be recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side, you must insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; if the break is in the left mandible, insert your index finger of the right hand and gently push it inside, then adjust it evenly with the other hand from outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break in the mandible is dislocated at two joints, then you must administer extension of two parts until it is equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movements of the teeth occur, or rupture, hold them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then place a bandage on the broken jaw and place .i. double cloth over it; and place over the cloth a large well-made splint, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and attach it above the muzzle that you can, and command the patient to rest, and nourish light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the figure changes, dislocate it on the third day and then reposition what has changed; place a plaster over it with flour from the mill mixed with egg or flour from a sieve, after you have removed the bandage; and place light linen over the plaster, and if the position of the patient does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it heals within four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come up, bring what we have said before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, observe that no piece of the bone has been removed; it requires subtle instruments suitable for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrowed, expand (it) with fire according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have removed all the pieces and none remain, then stitch (the) wound if it is wide, and place on it one plaster suitable for this purpose to promote healing until it heals.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks multiple times towards the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways: either it is broken and dislocated in two places, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when there is a fracture with an open wound, that you have two attendants, one holding the shoulder where the force breaks, and the other stretches the neck towards the affected area; then place the dislocation in your hands so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you need to extend further, place a round ball of fabric or linen over the patient's shoulder, as thick as necessary; stretch and tie the force (the fracture), hold the ball with your hand, and align the dislocation as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder outwards due to it being fully closed, then the patient must lie on their affected side and place one hand under the shoulder; and push the shoulder downwards, until the bones of the socket are raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the fracture to your fingers, and if you find debris, then it is necessary that you cut across [the bone]; and draw out the pieces gently, and if the bones cannot join due to any hindrance, then crush it at one of the incisions you have made; but place this instrument under the socket to hold it in place.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and resemble a spoon, but not concave, and be of such width as is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of your hand; and have two prongs, as you see, and one wide and the other narrow, as is the opening of the wound that you made when treating the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are certain of the abscess being hot, if it opens up, and the wound is small, or you doubt that it is a hot abscess, then use linen cloths and bandages on the wound, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if it is hot abscesses that come, soak one linen cloth in rose oil, asafetida and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The straining of the bone, when it has wounds and is cut open, is that you place the bandage of milled powder and egg yolk on the bone, and put light stops under it, and put a spear beneath the strain, if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very large bandage, one palm wide, then put a double cloth dampened on it, and wrap it; then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the end of the bandage is hanging.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage around the neck, and under the wound, and under the patient's healthy side; and tighten it from both sides, and when you see that the fracture aligns properly, and you can clearly see that the stick does not move over the broken bone, then keep it in place every day, and whenever the swelling lessens, hold it firmly.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under his wound to lift the shoulder up; this will align the fracture by moving the shoulder blade together, or tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it except in case of bad accident, for 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then perform the traction, if necessary, and hold it in place until it is restored; and it is usually restored within 28 days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It often happens that the broken or dislocated shoulder does not heal without treatment; it should only be approached through touch (surgery). The shoulder should be arranged according to the shape of the fracture and reset in its natural form, in every possible way; then apply powder from the mill with egg whites and light plasters, and place two layers of cloth over it; then place a wide and thin stick, slightly larger than the shoulder, under the shoulder (or where the shoulder was before); if there are no bones protruding, use flaxen plasters to cushion the stick so that it fits evenly. Then tightly bind the shoulder with a long bandage so that the stick does not move from its place, and watch it every day; whenever it swells, rebind it, and adjust the stick if it is out of place, and have the patient lie on his side. The shoulder will heal in 20 or 25 days, and when this number is reached, loosen it, but be careful as it is not bone that becomes dislocated easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone part protrudes in front and not under the skin, lift it up and cut it, and do as we have said to treat an abscess using hot cautery.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture (the) thigh
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The thigh is sometimes fractured in the middle, but it happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the sides. And when it is fractured internally, it slips downwards, causing the patient great pain, and lack of nourishment, and soon vomiting blood, and the wounds open in the fractured bone, and he feels nothing well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on their back, and one places a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two costal arches with both hands, subtlety adjusting it to be even in all ways possible, until the figure of the bone is as required; then put pressure bandages and poultices made of salt or a lighter material, and wrap it in one cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the limb round repeatedly, and tighten it gently, and examine every hour if it softens, if it becomes soft then tighten it again; and if it requires dislocation due to corrosion or itching at the location, or pain or abscess, hurry up, and dislocate it, remove the pressure bandage, and treat the one who has come with remedies of cures; then reset the pressure bandage and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the ribs fracture
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Note that the fracture of the ribs occurs only in large ones posterior to the back and at the neck inside, and they bend only because they are slippery; and it is well felt in the examination of the hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the re-setting is that you equalize the fracture, as it should be. Then place a splint, and hold it in place with a stick, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the rib fracture is inclined inside, the patient feels very great pain and shortness of breath, like pleurisy, for the bone pierces the flesh; the armpits swell, and they immediately vomit a large amount of blood, which is a serious illness, and the ancients have made many efforts to cure it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the stomach, in order to push the fracture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not allow hot irons to come if they have not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If they have come, make it healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said one of us puts blisters on the limb to ripen it, which seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the blisters attract excessive fluid to the limb due to its weak condition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said one should cover the limb with damp linen dipped in hot oil and place poultices between the ribs to make the swelling equal around it, then let it be treated with the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels intense pain that he cannot endure due to the broken bone and there is fear in the patient, then you must make an incision over the broken rib, and put an instrument under it for support; and then you should cut the bone lightly, and draw it out gently, and then sew the two sides of the wound, if it is large, and treat with healing ointment until it heals. And if an abscess comes, place wet cloths soaked in rose oil on it, and put it there; and cure the rib as much as necessary to deal with the abscess, and lie him down with his body on the side where it is broken until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes breaks occur in the bones of the neck, and sometimes it bends; and similarly with the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to anyone, and you wish to know if they will recover or not, if you see their hands becoming soft, swollen, and dead, and unable to move or stretch, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it. Know that they are mortal in various positions, and if they cannot speak and feel well when you press and prick, know that the jointure of the bone is saved, and that the patient can be cured if treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And when a similar thing happens to the spine in the back, and you wish to know if it will recover or not, beware if the feet are swollen, and injuries have occurred in the hands, and sudden movement and pain occur in the back without volition; and when it is provoked on the stomach, it occurs suddenly and without volition. And when it is prodded on the back and wishes to sit, it cannot. Know that it is mortal: do not labor at its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this accident does not happen, then it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward [the patient] if there is an abscess that is hot, you place on it rose oil or egg yolk oil until it is soothed; then put one of the soothing and drying plasters on top, bind it with a string, and command the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he recovers.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone dislocates, you must cover it with oil; then remove the bone, join the two edges of the wound together with a stitch, if it is large, until it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the head of the cow," put your left thumb in its place and hold it equal to your right hand, then apply the plaster and splint, if necessary; then tighten it, and if any bone dislocates again, you must fix it, remove the bone, and heal the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break of the thighbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it occurs, there is only a little lessening at the head; it becomes long, bends towards the groin, and comes to the patient pain at the place where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are over the break; and recognize what the break is and the shape of it; and if the break is only at the head, then make the break equal to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or it bends inside, then make the patient lie on his stomach until the restoration of that break is presented to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it even, place the splint on it, then place a stick or a yew branch on top and hold the fracture so it does not move; and press the joint beneath the ribs until they are equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If an abscess has broken out, do not touch it until it is soothed, and place what we have previously mentioned on top of it; then return to treatment, and hold it as needed, if there is no bad event; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	the shoulder blade is that which is between the ribs and the neck of the upper arm, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of two manners: one of which is that you take a rod thicker than your little finger, according to this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two heads together with two rods, and pass them over the top, and place the patient on one seat; then lower his broken arm onto the rod, until it reaches the shoulder joint, and attach a splint of rod in the middle, then raise it above some heavy object or have the ministers extend it below; then place the mirrors the breaker's hands together, until the breaker returns as required.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way it is that one binds the patient on his bed, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two assistants that one holds where it is above the break with his hands, and the others hold below all the way, and each extends to their respective parts.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the extraction is stronger, bind one rope below the break, and above the break, and each assistant extends to their respective parts. And if the break is near the neck of the shoulder, you must place a middle rope below the buttock, and another towards the cost, below the break; and in the same way, if the break is towards the cost, you must place a light rope without effort, such that the break is even on its level, and on the cost; then make it even, as needed, and hold it, unless an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess does come, do not hold it for more than 7 days, and put soft linen with rose oil on it until the abscess is soothed; then hold it, and the method of holding it is that you place a plaster on the break, then raise the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or chest; and hold the cloth, and hold it on the shoulder, and on the arm, such that the arm is in a straight line, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is moving, use splints, and place a larger and stronger splint above the fracture, with one inch of space between each splint, and let each splint be large enough to pass over the fracture by two inches on each side; then hold the splints as I have said at the beginning of the chapter regarding the fracture, more firmly and less in loosening.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the position of the splints and the tightening, as we have said, during the time you are setting the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess has healed, let it remain bound for seven days, as we have said; then look every three days at the binding, to ensure no pus or inflammation appears at the site, nor can the blood circulation reach the limb because it is too tight. If it swells, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	If no such accident occurs, do not remove the binding before four or more days have passed, and let the patient lie on their back with their hands on their stomach; place one evenly woven cloth cushion under the shoulder, and watch every hour of the day or night that the fracture site does not move or become softened, or loosens the bindings. If it swells due to the power of medicine, give them the meat that we have mentioned before, in such a way that the meat is first finely ground; and when it begins to heal, let it grow thicker. It is customary for the shoulder and arm to be repositioned within 40 days of the injury; and then they should be released and given warm baths and medicines with onions to further improve the site. If the wound is ugly and filled, wait one day or two months before removing the binding.
de la brisure du bras	Of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of two bones which are called the "forearm," of which one is small and it's the one that forms the wrist; and the other is large, and it's the one that is below, towards the little finger; by chance, only the large forearm can break, or only the small one, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small forearm is broken, restoration and healing are easy; but when the large one is broken, healing is difficult, and more troublesome than when both are broken together. If it's only the small forearm that breaks, then it should be slightly extended lightly and set straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the large forearm that breaks, then it should be pulled stronger; and extend it by one inch and raise the wrist of the hand higher than the others, and the small finger lower than the others, and cross the patient over himself, and a splint in front of him higher than the patient does not suffer any pain; then the ministers stretch their arms above the broken part to the underside or to one link, and another minister on the other side. And then set it straight by the surgeon according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is a fracture in several pieces, put each one back into its place; and if there is any displacement that pierces the skin which you cannot restore to its place, cut off and remove the bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if it is with the break causing an open wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; take care for its treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the restoration there appear abscesses covered by pus, apply one piece of cloth made of rose oil and white beeswax that is neither too hard nor too soft; and cover it subtly with one cloth. Then remove the ointment, and apply the plaster made from the powder of the mill along with egg white. Afterwards put on the splints, and the splints for the break should be more prominent at the break than elsewhere, and a little larger than the others; and know that it must have 7 splints or more according to the different positions: whether the break is in one bone or two; and bind more tightly above the break than elsewhere, but less when aligning, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths covering the break be soft and moist, not too hard or abrasive; and let the threads that hold it be made of flax, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And check the limb and the ligament afterwards after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accidents happen to the limb, such as itching that happens to the limb, then you must soak the limb in warm water until the itching is eased; and let the limb not rest. Then start the binding again, and if the ligaments are damaged and the bones dislocated, and similar things, advise accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If the urine cannot reach the limb because it is too narrow, then you must soften it for a short while and let it be for some days until the urine flows through it, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If none of the things that we have mentioned come to the patient, then do not release him until twenty days have passed. Or if inquiries are made about it during this time, then tie his hands to his neck and make his necks even, and keep him from movement and turning over, and let him sleep on his back; know that this fracture is healed in thirty or thirty-five days, and possibly in twenty days according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	In the back of the hand and at the knuckles there are few breaks, and they occur many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the sole of the hand is broken or fractured, the patient should lie flat on his back and stretch out straight in front of him equally; then place his hand above a cloth and extend the broken bones, aligning them with mirrors, until they are well joined; apply a plaster and wadding if an abscess does not appear, then apply a splint according to the size of the fracture; and it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the back of the sole near the belly of the foot, make a splint from cloths and instruct the patient to strap his broken foot to it; then fasten a long cloth, and the splint should be as large as the palm of the hand, and strain it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is open, then you should place a splint above and another one below in the sole, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and compress the ligament between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If a fracture occurs in any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, you should make it even as necessary; and hold it with the sole, and if you see that you place a straight small splint to lift the fracture, and do not move; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, you should make them even, and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or tie all of them in one place, which is better, or place a splint on it, as for the thumb; and take care in the restoration and placement of the abscess heat, and treat those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	fractured shin
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the shin are often broken, and it is easily seen when they twist forward and backward; and the restoration [of the bone] is that one tie [a splint] is placed above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his back, then each minister extends their tie evenly to their respective parts; and this is when the break is at the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	If the break is near the root of the shin, one of the ties should be towards the ankle, and the other ties below the break. And if it is near the knee, then the ties should be beside the knee, and the extension should be downwards; then have the ministers align the bone with their two hands, according to its natural shape, and then apply the splint and bind, as long as there is no abscess present.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess heated (treated with heat), let it be allowed to cool down before returning to your work and treatment; the procedure is carried out in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap above the fracture (the broken bone), that is, a thick bandage doubled in two or three layers, and let the superfluous parts remain; then turn the leg so the heels come to the root of the thigh, and insert one long thread between the thigh and the leg, under the knee, and bring the end of the thread above; then turn the leg and the bandage upwards on the thigh and the calf, then place a splint over the fracture and place a splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to keep the alignment straight, then begin to bind firmly for four or five turns above the splint; and as you go up above the splint, loosen it; then take the two threads that you inserted between the leg and the thigh, and tie four splints above them, then go under the thread below, so that you come to the foot; tighten it, so that the bone does not move from its place, then leave it thus, so that no abscess or swelling or similar thing appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is a swelling or any piece of the bone that protrudes, you should cut it off if possible; and if not, you should break the area and draw out the pus; and treat it as we have said before until it heals completely.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the leg is broken in such a way as if one sets a splint, as in the shoulder or arm; however, during restoration, it does not harm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the leg is restored within one day, or a little more or less, according to the differences in complexion.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the leg (genuine)
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the leg (genuine) there is little breakage, but it bends frequently. And if it breaks, it is not a complete fracture, but rather a crack or puncture, and it causes all pain, and pain everywhere, and this is felt by everyone.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is this: When equalizing the bone that is broken to its place, it should be assembled as much as possible; then put the splint, and place a round stick there if needed, and hold it in place as necessary, then check all the arrangements that we have said in other fractures, such as abscess heat and similar things; apply to each accident what is required, until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "shinbone" and the others are called "fibula"; and it happens just like a fracture comes to the arm, and for this reason, the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the work is all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fine bone is broken, it bends forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and can be seen; then it bends under. Bring extension to it, make it even, and tie the edges equally; however, if the break is misaligned and there are multiple pieces, the extension should be smaller and lighter; align it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two handfuls of straw that cover the leg from one side and the other, and be as long as the leg from the knee to below; then wrap it in two layers, one on top and one underneath, and tie it in the middle so that the leg cannot tilt to the right or left, and this is good; and no one should place one bandage of the length of the leg, and it should be of straw, and place the leg for protection against movement, and do this at the break where there is pain; move the leg every day to see if there is abscess or other accident; cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no break of bones, but at times there is a break in the foot and toes, and it does not occur often except in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the foot bones, and you see these bones rising one above the other, put the patient on his back on the ground, as if he wants to go, then place your foot on top of the injured one where the bones have risen, then press it until they return to their place; then apply a splint and bandage, and put a small plank under the foot with two flat pieces, then tighten the bandage around the foot in the usual way, after you have wrapped fabric around it, and other things that are needed.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, remove the bandage as you will find the bones even, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two bones are broken, restore them as we have said about the hand bones; then set a splint on the broken bone according to the length of the bone, and it should be slightly larger, then place a table beneath the splinted area as I have said, and apply pressure as needed; and if there are more than 2, or 3, or more broken bones, set a splint on each one according to their quantity, wrapped in one linen cloth, and hold the table beneath the splinted area; and it should be positioned so that it covers the belly of the bone, so that it touches well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not neglect the other things I have said about other fractures, after what has been said; and treat each case according to its need.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the wrist bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the female nature is broken, make her sit upright, then incline her towards the part of the back and hold her from behind; then fill the hollow with cotton, and put in it as big a stone as one can; then turn the woman over, and draw down the small of her back bit by bit, and when the cotton comes to the entrance of the nature, the bone returns with the stone; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for 7 days or more: the break will be restored. If you see, take a bladder of brambles, tie one end to the perineum, and push the entire bladder into the nature; then blow forcefully into the tube until the bladder is inflated within: the break will return to its place; then fill it with cotton, and leave it for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the thumb joint of either man or woman is broken, restore it in the same way as we have said for the bone of the forearm; and these breaks should not be hidden from him who applies his study and skill to them, and pays attention to my book. For the breaks indicate a variety of ways for restoration: therefore, take note of this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of a broken penis, take a goose's gullet and insert the penis into it; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for 3 or more days, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breakage with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For that one who has breakage with wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the leg or shoulder or something similar, he must be bandaged now, so that the bandages that we have said bear witness to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, then anoint it with vinegar, if you do not have anything else, then proceed to restore the breakage in that same hour, or on that day, if abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, because you would cause a bad event to happen.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks and appears exposed at the edge of the wound, you must gently set it in place with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the fractured bone pieces do not align themselves to be set in place by your hands, you must use this instrument which is made of iron, about 7 or 8 inches long, and as wide as the size of the wound; and for this reason, the mirror should grasp 3 or 4 (depending on what is required in each case of fracture), and it should be round and somewhat large but not too thin so that it does not bend during your work on the limb, and it should be sharp at the front end and thick from the middle to the tip, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	This instrument is called "palainche", so you should place the curved pieces of bone on top of the exposed bone; and press it once until it lines up, ensuring they are equal in length. If the fracture is fine and the instrument cannot grasp the bone properly, you must cut the edge of the bone to give the instrument enough grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, strike it with an appropriate instrument, either chisel or saw, to your power; then remove that which is left in the bone by sharp cutting and small scrapes.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone has been reset and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. Make it so that it is in its natural position, then moisten a clean cloth with black stiptic wine, if available; and do not put any oil or other substance over the wound where there is an ulcer, as it will cause pus and corruption; then apply splints when you have restored the bone, leave the wound open, cover the edges all around, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not compressed with a fracture; and many times this has been done by foolish surgeons, causing harm or death to the patient, or causing some infection sometimes; and the splints should be softer and more flexible than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	If the wound is bad or large, and you fear that some mishap may come from it, as we have said, and you feel pain at the site, do not put splints on; instead wrap around, in place of splints, hard cloths, and bind them. And when you see after one day or two days swelling at the wound, remove what you have put over it with all vinegar, and apply ointment for healing wounds, such as ointment for festering sores and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the member twice a day, at morning and evening, as long as it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be placed so that the bone moves down gently towards the inside.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it passes many days and the bone cannot heal but goes down again, since there are small fragments of bones, you must try to cure the wound and remove all those loose fragments that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if an ulcer or any other kind of corruption comes to the place, you must cure it, according to what he said in his previous chapter. And when a bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and similar large limbs, do not drain it, for many times death comes, but leave it until it can heal; perhaps it will heal by itself after twenty days or thirty, then cure the wound if possible; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The arriving blisters on the sores
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	There are often many times after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it is an unpleasant sight to see the shape of the limb; and unfortunately, the limbs cannot perform their natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, be careful if we are sick: administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and saracocola, acacia, and similar ones; so take any of these things or all together, and grind them with a sharp vinegar or with enough egg white or oil; then place it on the wound in poultices, and hold it tightly and do not remove it for many days; and then open it, and start another one, until the node is removed; or you can apply a well-made wooden plank, because the properties of wood are that it removes all inflammations from limbs. If the node has turned into hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, then you chop it off with a knife, and make the excess apparent; or you scrape it with any rasp, until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak limb after care
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.
